31&#160;July&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="#cite_note-Airbus_O_D-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span class="nowrap">Program cost</span>\n</th>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac15 billion (Airbus 2015)<sup id="cite_ref-TG150118_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TG150118-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> to \xe2\x82\xac25 billion (2016 estimate)<sup id="cite_ref-BB160712_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BB160712-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span class="nowrap">Unit cost</span>\n</th>\n<td><div>\n<span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>445.6 million</span> (2018)<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_prices_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_prices-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></div>\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n</tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Airbus A380</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Double-deck_aircraft" title="Double-deck aircraft">double-deck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body</a>, four-engine <a href="/wiki/Jet_airliner" title="Jet airliner">jet airliner</a> manufactured by European manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It is the world\'s largest passenger airliner, and the airports at which it operates have upgraded facilities to accommodate it.  It was initially named <b>Airbus A3XX</b> and designed to challenge <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>\'s monopoly in the large-aircraft market. The A380 made its first flight on 27 April 2005 and entered commercial service on 25 October 2007 with <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a>. An improved version, the A380plus, is under development.\n</p><p>The A380\'s upper deck extends along the entire length of the <a href="/wiki/Fuselage" title="Fuselage">fuselage</a>; it is narrower than the lower deck but remains comparable to the width of other wide-body aircraft. This gives the A380-800\'s <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_cabin" title="Aircraft cabin">cabin</a> 550 square metres (5,920&#160;sq&#160;ft) of usable floor space,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> 40% more than the next largest airliner, the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8" title="Boeing 747-8">Boeing 747-8</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and provides seating for 525 people in a typical three-<a href="/wiki/Travel_class" title="Travel class">class</a> configuration or up to 853 people in an all-<a href="/wiki/Economy_class" title="Economy class">economy class</a> configuration. The A380-800 has a design <a href="/wiki/Range_(aeronautics)" title="Range (aeronautics)">range</a> of 8,500 nautical miles (15,700&#160;km), serving the <a href="/wiki/Longest_flights#Currently_scheduled_(top_30,_by_distance)" title="Longest flights">third- and fifth-longest non-stop scheduled flights</a> in the world (as of November 2017), and a <a href="/wiki/Cruising_speed" class="mw-redirect" title="Cruising speed">cruising speed</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mach_number" title="Mach number">Mach</a>&#160;0.85 (about 900&#160;km/h, 560&#160;mph or 490&#160;kt at <a href="/wiki/Cruising_altitude" class="mw-redirect" title="Cruising altitude">cruising altitude</a>).\n</p><p>As of  July&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Airbus had received 331 firm orders and delivered 229 aircraft; <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> is the biggest A380 customer with 162 ordered of which 104 have been delivered.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_O_D_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_O_D-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" href="#Orders_and_deliveries"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Orders and deliveries</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Timeline"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Timeline</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Operators"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Operators</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Notable_routes"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Notable routes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Incidents_and_accidents"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Incidents and accidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#Specifications"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Specifications</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="floatright">\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_1290fa2f97c41e4f5e474b48e593d021"></map><img usemap="#timeline_1290fa2f97c41e4f5e474b48e593d021" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/1290fa2f97c41e4f5e474b48e593d021.png" /></div>\n</div>\n<p>In mid-1988, Airbus engineers led by Jean Roeder began work in secret on the development of an ultra-high-capacity airliner (UHCA), both to complete its own range of products and to break the dominance that <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> had enjoyed in this market segment since the early 1970s with its <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">747</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas" title="McDonnell Douglas">McDonnell Douglas</a> unsuccessfully offered its smaller, double-deck <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-12" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-12">MD-12</a> concept for sale.<sup id="cite_ref-MDC_brochure_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MDC_brochure-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Roeder was given approval for further evaluations of the UHCA after a formal presentation to the President and <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> in June 1990. The <a href="/wiki/Megaproject" title="Megaproject">megaproject</a> was announced at the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Farnborough_Airshow" title="Farnborough Airshow">Farnborough Airshow</a>, with the stated goal of 15% lower operating costs than the 747-400.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Airbus organised four teams of designers, one from each of its partners (<a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9rospatiale" title="A\xc3\xa9rospatiale">A\xc3\xa9rospatiale</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace" title="British Aerospace">British Aerospace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Aerospace_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Deutsche Aerospace AG">Deutsche Aerospace AG</a>, <a href="/wiki/EADS_CASA" title="EADS CASA">CASA</a>) to propose new technologies for its future aircraft designs. The designs were presented in 1992 and the most competitive designs were used.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 1993, Boeing and several companies in the Airbus consortium started a joint feasibility study of a Very Large Commercial Transport (VLCT), aiming to form a partnership to share the limited market.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SeattlePIoverview_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SeattlePIoverview-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> This joint study was abandoned two years later, Boeing\'s interest having declined because analysts thought that such a product was unlikely to cover the projected $15 billion development cost. Despite the fact that only two airlines had expressed public interest in purchasing such a plane, Airbus was already pursuing its own large-plane project. Analysts suggested that Boeing would instead pursue stretching its 747 design, and that air travel was already moving away from the <a href="/wiki/Spoke-hub_distribution_paradigm" class="mw-redirect" title="Spoke-hub distribution paradigm">hub-and-spoke</a> system that consolidated traffic into large planes, and toward more non-stop routes that could be served by smaller planes.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 1994, Airbus announced its plan to develop its own very large airliner, designated as A3XX.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Airbus considered several designs, including an unusual side-by-side combination of two fuselages from its <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340" title="Airbus A340">A340</a>, the largest Airbus jet at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-norris_wagner_book_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris_wagner_book-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The A3XX was pitted against the VLCT study and Boeing\'s own <a href="/wiki/Boeing_NLA" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing NLA">New Large Aircraft</a> successor to the 747.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> From 1997 to 2000, as the <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="East Asian financial crisis">East Asian financial crisis</a> darkened the market outlook, Airbus refined its design, targeting a 15\xe2\x80\x9320% reduction in operating costs over the existing Boeing 747\xe2\x80\x93400. The A3XX design converged on a double-decker layout that provided more passenger volume than a traditional single-deck design,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> in line with traditional hub-and-spoke theory as opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Point-to-point_transit" title="Point-to-point transit">point-to-point theory</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Aerlines_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aerlines-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> after conducting an extensive market analysis with over 200 <a href="/wiki/Focus_group" title="Focus group">focus groups</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ms_a380_debate_20060905_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ms_a380_debate_20060905-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LeehamLawler_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeehamLawler-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Although early marketing of the huge cross-section touted the possibility of duty-free shops, restaurant-like dining, gyms, casinos and beauty parlours on board, the realities of airline economics have kept such dreams grounded.\n</p><p>On 19 December 2000, the supervisory board of newly restructured Airbus voted to launch an \xe2\x82\xac8.8-billion programme to build the A3XX, re-designated as the A380,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> with 50 firm orders from six launch customers.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The A380 designation was a break from previous Airbus families, which had progressed sequentially from A300 to A340. It was chosen because the number 8 resembles the double-deck cross section, and is a <a href="/wiki/Numbers_in_Chinese_culture#Eight" class="mw-redirect" title="Numbers in Chinese culture">lucky number</a> in some Asian countries where the aircraft was being marketed.<sup id="cite_ref-norris_wagner_book_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris_wagner_book-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The aircraft configuration was finalised in early 2001, and manufacturing of the first A380 wing-box component started on 23 January 2002. The development cost of the A380 had grown to \xe2\x82\xac11\xe2\x80\x9314<sup id="cite_ref-esar_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-esar-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>&#160;billion when the first aircraft was completed.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Total_development_cost">Total development cost</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Total development cost">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2000, the originally projected development cost was \xe2\x82\xac9.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Lib\xc3\xa9120507_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lib\xc3\xa9120507-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 2004 Airbus estimated 1.5 billion euros ($2 billion) would be added for a \xe2\x82\xac10.3 Bn ($12.7 Bn) total.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In 2006 at \xe2\x82\xac10.2 Billion, Airbus stopped publishing its reported cost and then provisioned \xe2\x82\xac4.9 Bn after the difficulties in electric cabling and two years delay for an estimated total of \xe2\x82\xac18 Bn.<sup id="cite_ref-Lib\xc3\xa9120507_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lib\xc3\xa9120507-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, the aircraft was estimated to have cost $25bn (\xc2\xa316bn \xe2\x80\x93 \xe2\x82\xac18.9bn) to develop.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Airbus said development costs were \xe2\x82\xac15bn (\xc2\xa311.4bn \xe2\x80\x93 $16.95 Bn), though analysts believe the figure is likely to be at least \xe2\x82\xac5bn ($5.65 Bn) more for a \xe2\x82\xac20 Bn ($22.6 Bn) total.<sup id="cite_ref-TG150118_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TG150118-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, The A380 development costs were estimated at $25 billion for 15 years,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> $25\xe2\x80\x9330 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> or 25 billion euros ($28 billion).<sup id="cite_ref-BB160712_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BB160712-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To start the program in 2000, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/U.K." class="mw-redirect" title="U.K.">U.K.</a> loaned Airbus 3.5 billion euros and refundable advances reached 5.9 billion euros ($7.3 billion).\nIn February 2018, after an Emirates order secured production of the unprofitable program for ten years, Airbus revised its deal with these countries to save $1.4 billion (17%): restructured terms allow to lower the production rate from eight in 2019 to six per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg23feb2018_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg23feb2018-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Transport_A380_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="Diagram showing flow of aircraft part in western Europe. Land is white, sea is pale blue" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Transport_A380_en.svg/230px-Transport_A380_en.svg.png" width="230" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Transport_A380_en.svg/345px-Transport_A380_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Transport_A380_en.svg/460px-Transport_A380_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="915" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Transport_A380_en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geographical logistics sequence for the A380, with final assembly in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Major structural sections of the A380 are built in France, Germany, Spain, and the United Kingdom. Due to the sections\' large size, traditional transportation methods proved unfeasible,<sup id="cite_ref-moral_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moral-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> so they are brought to the <i>Jean-Luc Lagard\xc3\xa8re Plant</i> assembly hall in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, France, by specialised road and water transportation, though some parts are moved by the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Beluga" title="Airbus Beluga">A300-600ST <i>Beluga</i></a> transport aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> A380 components are provided by suppliers from around the world; the four largest contributors, by value, are <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolls-Royce plc">Rolls-Royce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safran" title="Safran">Safran</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Technologies_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="United Technologies Corporation">United Technologies</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ms_a380_debate_20060905_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ms_a380_debate_20060905-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For the surface movement of large A380 structural components, a complex route known as the <a href="/wiki/Itin%C3%A9raire_%C3%A0_Grand_Gabarit" title="Itin\xc3\xa9raire \xc3\xa0 Grand Gabarit">Itin\xc3\xa9raire \xc3\xa0 Grand Gabarit</a> was developed. This involved the construction of a fleet of <a href="/wiki/Roll-on/roll-off" title="Roll-on/roll-off">roll-on/roll-off</a> (RORO) ships and barges, the construction of port facilities and the development of new and modified roads to accommodate oversized road convoys.<sup id="cite_ref-aw200905_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aw200905-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The front and rear fuselage sections are shipped on one of three RORO ships from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> in northern Germany to the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The wings are manufactured at <a href="/wiki/Broughton,_Flintshire" title="Broughton, Flintshire">Broughton</a> in North Wales, then transported by <a href="/wiki/Barge" title="Barge">barge</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mostyn" title="Mostyn">Mostyn</a> docks for ship transport.<sup id="cite_ref-fi_20030520_production_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi_20030520_production-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_transport_Port_de_Bordeaux.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/A380_transport_Port_de_Bordeaux.jpg/220px-A380_transport_Port_de_Bordeaux.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/A380_transport_Port_de_Bordeaux.jpg/330px-A380_transport_Port_de_Bordeaux.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/A380_transport_Port_de_Bordeaux.jpg/440px-A380_transport_Port_de_Bordeaux.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="532" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_transport_Port_de_Bordeaux.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A380 components on a barge</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Saint-Nazaire" title="Saint-Nazaire">Saint-Nazaire</a> in western France, the ship exchanges the fuselage sections from Hamburg for larger, assembled sections, some of which include the nose. The ship unloads in <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>. The ship then picks up the belly and tail sections from <a href="/wiki/Construcciones_Aeron%C3%A1uticas_SA" title="Construcciones Aeron\xc3\xa1uticas SA">Construcciones Aeron\xc3\xa1uticas SA</a> in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="C\xc3\xa1diz">C\xc3\xa1diz</a> in southern Spain, and delivers them to Bordeaux. From there, the A380 parts are transported by barge to <a href="/wiki/Langon,_Gironde" title="Langon, Gironde">Langon</a>, and by oversize road convoys to the assembly hall in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-A380_convoys_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380_convoys-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In order to avoid damage from direct handling, parts are secured in custom jigs carried on self-powered wheeled vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-moral_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moral-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After assembly, the aircraft are flown to <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Finkenwerder_Airport" title="Hamburg Finkenwerder Airport">Hamburg Finkenwerder Airport</a> (XFW) to be furnished and painted. Airbus sized the production facilities and <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain" title="Supply chain">supply chain</a> for a production rate of four A380s per month.<sup id="cite_ref-fi_20030520_production_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi_20030520_production-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Testing">Testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_Reveal_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/A380_Reveal_1.jpg/220px-A380_Reveal_1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/A380_Reveal_1.jpg/330px-A380_Reveal_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/A380_Reveal_1.jpg/440px-A380_Reveal_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_Reveal_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first completed A380 at the "A380 Reveal" event in Toulouse, France, 18 January 2005</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1er_vol_de_l%27_A380.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/1er_vol_de_l%27_A380.jpg/220px-1er_vol_de_l%27_A380.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/1er_vol_de_l%27_A380.jpg/330px-1er_vol_de_l%27_A380.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/1er_vol_de_l%27_A380.jpg/440px-1er_vol_de_l%27_A380.jpg 2x" data-file-width="531" data-file-height="380" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1er_vol_de_l%27_A380.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A380 prototype on its <a href="/wiki/Maiden_flight" title="Maiden flight">maiden flight</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Five A380s were built for testing and demonstration purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_test_2005_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_test_2005-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The first A380, <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_registration" title="Aircraft registration">registered</a> <i>F-WWOW</i>, was unveiled in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a> 18 January 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> It first flew on 27 April 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-first_flight_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first_flight-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> This plane, equipped with <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Trent_900" title="Rolls-Royce Trent 900">Rolls-Royce Trent 900</a> engines, flew from <a href="/wiki/Toulouse%E2%80%93Blagnac_Airport" title="Toulouse\xe2\x80\x93Blagnac Airport">Toulouse\xe2\x80\x93Blagnac Airport</a> with a crew of six headed by chief <a href="/wiki/Test_pilot" title="Test pilot">test pilot</a> <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Rosay" title="Jacques Rosay">Jacques Rosay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Rosay said flying the A380 had been "like handling a bicycle".<sup id="cite_ref-First_flight_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_flight-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 December 2005, the A380 achieved its maximum design speed of Mach&#160;0.96, (its design cruise speed is Mach&#160;0.85) in a shallow dive.<sup id="cite_ref-flight_test_2005_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight_test_2005-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, the A380 flew its first high-altitude test at <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa_Bole_International_Airport" title="Addis Ababa Bole International Airport">Addis Ababa Bole International Airport</a>. It conducted its second high-altitude test at the same airport in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On 10 January 2006, it flew to <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_C%C3%B3rdova_International_Airport" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada C\xc3\xb3rdova International Airport">Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada C\xc3\xb3rdova International Airport</a> in Colombia, accomplishing the transatlantic testing, and then it went to <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado International Airport</a> to test the engine operation in high-altitude airports. It arrived in North America on 6 February 2006, landing in <a href="/wiki/Iqaluit" title="Iqaluit">Iqaluit</a>, Nunavut in Canada for cold-weather testing.<sup id="cite_ref-Cold_weather_test_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cold_weather_test-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_teststation_fb06rs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/A380_teststation_fb06rs.jpg/220px-A380_teststation_fb06rs.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/A380_teststation_fb06rs.jpg/330px-A380_teststation_fb06rs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/A380_teststation_fb06rs.jpg/440px-A380_teststation_fb06rs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1428" data-file-height="1071" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_teststation_fb06rs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flight_test_engineer" title="Flight test engineer">Flight test engineer</a>\'s station on the lower deck of A380 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A380_orders_and_deliveries#Production_List" title="List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries">F-WWOW</a></div></div></div>\n<p>On 14 February 2006, during the destructive wing strength certification test on <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A380_orders_and_deliveries#Production_List" title="List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries">MSN5000</a>, the test wing of the A380 failed at 145% of the limit load, short of the required 150% level. Airbus announced modifications adding 30&#160;kg (66&#160;lb) to the wing to provide the required strength.<sup id="cite_ref-A380_wing_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380_wing-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On 26 March 2006, the A380 underwent evacuation certification in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>. With 8 of the 16 exits <a href="/wiki/Arbitrariness" title="Arbitrariness">arbitrarily</a> blocked, 853 mixed passengers and 20 crew exited the darkened aircraft in 78 seconds, less than the 90 seconds required for certification.<sup id="cite_ref-evacuation_test_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evacuation_test-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, the A380 received <a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">European Aviation Safety Agency</a> (EASA) and United States <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a> (FAA) approval to carry up to 853 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-evacuation_test_2_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evacuation_test_2-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first A380 using <a href="/wiki/Engine_Alliance_GP7200" class="mw-redirect" title="Engine Alliance GP7200">GP7200</a> engines\xe2\x80\x94serial number <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A380_orders_and_deliveries#Production_List" title="List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries">MSN009</a> and registration <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A380_orders_and_deliveries#Production_List" title="List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries">F-WWEA</a>\xe2\x80\x94flew on 25 August 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> On 4 September 2006, the first full passenger-carrying flight test took place.<sup id="cite_ref-first_pax_flight_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first_pax_flight-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The aircraft flew from Toulouse with 474 Airbus employees on board, in a test of passenger facilities and comfort.<sup id="cite_ref-first_pax_flight_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first_pax_flight-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> In November 2006, a further series of route-proving flights demonstrated the aircraft\'s performance for 150 flight hours under typical airline operating conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-A380testfly_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380testfly-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the A380 test aircraft continue to perform test procedures.<sup id="cite_ref-whe_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whe-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus obtained <a href="/wiki/Type_certificate" title="Type certificate">type certificates</a> for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A380_orders_and_deliveries#Models" title="List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries">A380-841</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A380_orders_and_deliveries#Models" title="List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries">A380-842</a> model from the EASA and FAA on 12 December 2006 in a joint ceremony at the company\'s French headquarters,<sup id="cite_ref-EASA_A380_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EASA_A380-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FAA_A380_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA_A380-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> receiving the <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization" title="International Civil Aviation Organization">ICAO</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_ICAO_aircraft_type_designators" title="List of ICAO aircraft type designators">code</a> A388.<sup id="cite_ref-icaoCode_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icaoCode-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A380_orders_and_deliveries#Models" title="List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries">A380-861</a> model obtained its type certificate on 14 December 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FAA_A380_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA_A380-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_and_delivery_delays">Production and delivery delays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Production and delivery delays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Second_floor.A-380_(4020687953).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Second_floor.A-380_%284020687953%29.jpg/220px-Second_floor.A-380_%284020687953%29.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Second_floor.A-380_%284020687953%29.jpg/330px-Second_floor.A-380_%284020687953%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Second_floor.A-380_%284020687953%29.jpg/440px-Second_floor.A-380_%284020687953%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="788" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Second_floor.A-380_(4020687953).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Naked cabin for flight tests with water tanks ballast</div></div></div>\n<p>Initial production of the A380 was troubled by delays attributed to the 530&#160;km (330&#160;mi) of wiring in each aircraft. Airbus cited as underlying causes the complexity of the cabin wiring (98,000 wires and 40,000 connectors), its concurrent design and production, the high degree of customisation for each airline, and failures of <a href="/wiki/Configuration_management" title="Configuration management">configuration management</a> and <a href="/wiki/Change_control" title="Change control">change control</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eads_airbus_forecast_20061019_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eads_airbus_forecast_20061019-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wiring_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiring-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The German and Spanish Airbus facilities continued to use <a href="/wiki/CATIA" title="CATIA">CATIA</a> version&#160;4, while British and French sites migrated to version&#160;5.<sup id="cite_ref-wiringdetailed_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiringdetailed-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> This caused overall configuration management problems, at least in part because wire harnesses manufactured using <a href="/wiki/Aluminum_wire" class="mw-redirect" title="Aluminum wire">aluminium</a> rather than copper conductors necessitated special design rules including non-standard dimensions and bend radii; these were not easily transferred between versions of the software.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus announced the first delay in June 2005 and notified airlines that deliveries would be delayed by six months.<sup id="cite_ref-wiringdetailed_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiringdetailed-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> This reduced the total number of planned deliveries by the end of 2009 from about 120 to 90\xe2\x80\x93100. On 13 June 2006, Airbus announced a second delay, with the delivery schedule slipping an additional six to seven months.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Although the first delivery was still planned before the end of 2006, deliveries in 2007 would drop to only 9 aircraft, and deliveries by the end of 2009 would be cut to 70\xe2\x80\x9380 aircraft. The announcement caused a 26% drop in the share price of Airbus\' parent, EADS,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and led to the departure of EADS CEO <a href="/wiki/No%C3%ABl_Forgeard" title="No\xc3\xabl Forgeard">No\xc3\xabl Forgeard</a>, Airbus CEO <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Humbert" title="Gustav Humbert">Gustav Humbert</a>, and A380 programme manager <a href="/wiki/Charles_Champion" title="Charles Champion">Charles Champion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wiringdetailed_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiringdetailed-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-management_shuffle_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-management_shuffle-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 3 October 2006, upon completion of a review of the A380 programme, Airbus CEO <a href="/wiki/Christian_Streiff" title="Christian Streiff">Christian Streiff</a> announced a third delay,<sup id="cite_ref-wiringdetailed_67-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiringdetailed-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> pushing the first delivery to October 2007, to be followed by 13 deliveries in 2008, 25 in 2009, and the full production rate of 45 aircraft per year in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-third_delay_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-third_delay-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The delay also increased the earnings shortfall projected by Airbus through 2010 to \xe2\x82\xac4.8&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-wiringdetailed_67-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiringdetailed-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-the_times_20061003_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_times_20061003-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As Airbus prioritised the work on the A380-800 over the A380F,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> freighter orders were cancelled by <a href="/wiki/FedEx" title="FedEx">FedEx</a><sup id="cite_ref-fedex_cancel_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fedex_cancel-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/United_Parcel_Service" title="United Parcel Service">United Parcel Service</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> or converted to A380-800 by Emirates and ILFC.<sup id="cite_ref-ILFC_A380F_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ILFC_A380F-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Airbus suspended work on the freighter version, but said it remained on offer,<sup id="cite_ref-a380f_freighterinterrupted_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a380f_freighterinterrupted-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> albeit without a service entry date.<sup id="cite_ref-no-timeline-on-the-a380-freighter_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-no-timeline-on-the-a380-freighter-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> For the passenger version Airbus negotiated a revised delivery schedule and compensation with the 13 customers, all of which retained their orders with some placing subsequent orders, including Emirates,<sup id="cite_ref-Emirates_Airlines_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Emirates_Airlines-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Singapore Airlines,<sup id="cite_ref-Singapore_Airlines_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singapore_Airlines-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Qantas,<sup id="cite_ref-Qantas_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Qantas-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Air France,<sup id="cite_ref-Air_France_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Air_France-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Qatar Airways,<sup id="cite_ref-Qatar_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Qatar-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> and Korean Air.<sup id="cite_ref-Korean_Air_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Korean_Air-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Beginning in 2007 the A380 was considered as a potential replacement for the existing <a href="/wiki/Boeing_VC-25" title="Boeing VC-25">Boeing VC-25</a> serving as <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a> presidential transport,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> but in January 2009 EADS declared that they were not going to bid for the contract, as assembling only three planes in the US would not make financial sense.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 May 2008, Airbus announced reduced deliveries for the years 2008 (12) and 2009 (21).<sup id="cite_ref-A380_production_ramp-up_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380_production_ramp-up-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> After further manufacturing setbacks, Airbus announced its plan to deliver 14 A380s in 2009, down from the previously revised target of 18.<sup id="cite_ref-new_schedule_18_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_schedule_18-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> A total of 10 A380s were delivered in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 Airbus delivered 18 of the expected 20 A380s, due to Rolls-Royce engine availability problems.<sup id="cite_ref-Deliveries_2010_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deliveries_2010-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Airbus planned to deliver "between 20 and 25" A380s in 2011 before ramping up to three a month in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Deliveries_2010_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deliveries_2010-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In fact, Airbus delivered 26 units, thus outdoing its predicted output for the first time. As of  July&#160;2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, production was 3 aircraft per month. Among the production problems are challenging interiors, interiors being installed sequentially rather than concurrently as in smaller planes, and union/government objections to streamlining.<sup id="cite_ref-wsjDMcc_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsjDMcc-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_rate">Production rate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Production rate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AIB_A380_F-WWSN!167_16mar15_LFBO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/AIB_A380_F-WWSN%21167_16mar15_LFBO.jpg/220px-AIB_A380_F-WWSN%21167_16mar15_LFBO.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/AIB_A380_F-WWSN%21167_16mar15_LFBO.jpg/330px-AIB_A380_F-WWSN%21167_16mar15_LFBO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/AIB_A380_F-WWSN%21167_16mar15_LFBO.jpg/440px-AIB_A380_F-WWSN%21167_16mar15_LFBO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5478" data-file-height="3630" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AIB_A380_F-WWSN!167_16mar15_LFBO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two A380s canceled by <a href="/wiki/Skymark" class="mw-redirect" title="Skymark">Skymark</a> and stored by Airbus</div></div></div>\n<p>At the July 2016 <a href="/wiki/Farnborough_Airshow" title="Farnborough Airshow">Farnborough Airshow</a> Airbus announced that in a \xe2\x80\x9cprudent, proactive step,\xe2\x80\x9d starting in 2018 it expects to deliver 12 A380 aircraft per year, down from 27 deliveries in 2015. The firm also warned production might slip back into red ink on each aircraft produced at that time, though it anticipates production will remain in the black for 2016 and 2017. \xe2\x80\x9cThe company will continue to improve the efficiency of its industrial system to achieve breakeven at 20 aircraft in 2017 and targets additional cost reduction initiatives to lower breakeven further.\xe2\x80\x9d<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Airbus expects that healthy demand for its other aircraft would allow it to avoid job losses from the cuts.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As Airbus expects to build 15 airliners in 2017 and 12 in 2018, Airbus Commercial Aircraft president <a href="/wiki/Fabrice_Br%C3%A9gier" title="Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier">Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier</a> said without orders in 2017 production should be reduced below one per month while remaining <a href="/wiki/Profitable" class="mw-redirect" title="Profitable">profitable</a> per unit and have the program continue for 20 to 30 years.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\nWithin its 2017 half-year report, Airbus adjusted 2019 deliveries to eight aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\nIn November 2017, its chief executive <a href="/wiki/Tom_Enders" title="Tom Enders">Tom Enders</a> was confident Airbus will still produce A380s in 2027 with more sales to come, and to further develop it to keep it competitive beyond 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\nAirbus was profitable at a rate of 15 per year and is trying to drive <a href="/wiki/Breakeven" class="mw-redirect" title="Breakeven">breakeven</a> down further but will make losses at eight per year.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek14nov2017_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek14nov2017-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> order for 36 could be finalised to keep it produced beyond 2020, but the airline wants guarantees the production will be maintained for 10 years, till 2028: reducing output to six a year would help to bridge that period and would support second-hand values while other buyers are approached, but the programme would still be unprofitable.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\nIf it fails to win the Emirates order, Airbus is ready to phase out its production gradually as it goes through its remaining orders until early 2020s.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters27dec2017_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters27dec2017-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To extend the program, Airbus offered China a production role in early 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\nWhile state owned airlines could order A380s, it would not help their low <a href="/wiki/Pricing" title="Pricing">yield</a> as it lowers frequency, they do not need more volume as <a href="/wiki/Widebody_aircraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Widebody aircraft">widebody aircraft</a> are already used on domestic routes and using the A380 on its intended long haul missions would free only a few <a href="/wiki/Airport_slot" class="mw-redirect" title="Airport slot">airport slots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After realising efficiencies to sustain production at a lower level, in 2017 Airbus delivered 15 "very close" to production breakeven while additional savings could continue as production is being further reduced: 12 should be delivered in 2018, eight in 2019 and six per year from 2020 with "digestible" losses.\nEnders is confident the A380 will gain additional orders from existing or new operators, and sees opportunities in Asia and particularly in China where it is "under-represented".<sup id="cite_ref-Flight16feb2018_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight16feb2018-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entry_into_service">Entry into service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Entry into service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Wallner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Singapore_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Wallner.jpg/220px-Singapore_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Wallner.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Singapore_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Wallner.jpg/330px-Singapore_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Wallner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Singapore_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Wallner.jpg/440px-Singapore_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Wallner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Wallner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> A380 at <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Z\xc3\xbcrich Airport">Z\xc3\xbcrich Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Nicknamed <i>Superjumbo</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-SJ_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-SJ-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> the first A380, MSN003 (registered as 9V-SKA), was delivered to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> on 15 October 2007 and entered service on 25 October 2007 with flight number SQ380 between <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Changi_Airport" title="Singapore Changi Airport">Singapore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Airport" title="Sydney Airport">Sydney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SeattlePIoverview_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SeattlePIoverview-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1st_SIA_flight_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1st_SIA_flight-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Passengers bought seats in a charity online auction paying between $560 and $100,380.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Two months later, Singapore Airlines CEO Chew Choong Seng stated the A380 was performing better than either the airline or Airbus had anticipated, burning 20% less fuel per seat-mile than the airline\'s <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">747\xe2\x80\x93400</a> fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-SIA&#39;s_Chew:_A380_pleases_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SIA&#39;s_Chew:_A380_pleases-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Emirates\' <a href="/wiki/Tim_Clark_(airline_executive)" title="Tim Clark (airline executive)">Tim Clark</a> claimed that the A380 has better fuel economy at Mach 0.86 than at 0.83,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> and that its technical dispatch reliability is at 97%, the same as Singapore Airlines. Airbus is committed to reach the industry standard of 98.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-techissu_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techissu-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> was the second airline to receive the A380 and commenced service between <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York</a> in August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1st_UAE_flight_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1st_UAE_flight-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">Qantas</a> followed, with flights between <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Airport" title="Melbourne Airport">Melbourne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a> in October 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-1st_QFA_flight_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1st_QFA_flight-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> By the end of 2008, 890,000 passengers had flown on 2,200 flights.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2009, the one millionth passenger was flown with Singapore Airlines<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> and by May of that year 1,500,000 passengers had flown on 4,200 flights.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> received its first A380 in October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> received its first A380 in May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> By July 2010, the 31 A380s then in service had transported 6 million passengers on 17,000 flights between 20 international destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus delivered the 100th A380 on 14 March 2013 to <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines" title="Malaysia Airlines">Malaysia Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In June 2014, over 65 million passengers had flown the A380,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> and more than 100 million passengers (averaging 375 per flight) by September 2015, with an <a href="/wiki/Availability" title="Availability">availability</a> of 98.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-awFlot2015-10-29_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awFlot2015-10-29-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Emirates stated that their A380 fleet had <a href="/wiki/Passenger_load_factor" title="Passenger load factor">load factors</a> of 90\xe2\x80\x93100%, and that the popularity of the aircraft with its passengers had not decreased in the past year.<sup id="cite_ref-fgLook_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fgLook-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Improvements_and_upgrades">Improvements and upgrades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Improvements and upgrades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2010, Airbus announced a new A380 build standard, incorporating a strengthened airframe structure and a 1.5\xc2\xb0 increase in <a href="/wiki/Wing_twist" title="Wing twist">wing twist</a>. Airbus will also offer, as an option, an improved maximum take-off weight, thus providing a better payload/range performance. Maximum take-off weight is increased by 4&#160;t (8,800&#160;lb), to 573&#160;t (1,263,000&#160;lb) and the range is extended by 100 nautical miles (190&#160;km); this is achieved by reducing flight loads, partly from optimising the fly-by-wire control laws.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> are the first two customers to have received this new option in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Emirates has asked for an update with new engines for the A380 to be competitive with the <a href="/wiki/777X" class="mw-redirect" title="777X">777X</a> around 2020, and Airbus is studying 11-abreast seating.<sup id="cite_ref-leeUp_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeUp-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, Airbus announced another increase in the A380\'s maximum take-off weight to 575&#160;t (1,268,000&#160;lb), a 6&#160;t increase from the initial A380 variant and 2&#160;t higher than the increased-weight proposal of 2010. Its range will increase by some 150 nautical miles (280&#160;km), taking its capability to around 8,350 nautical miles (15,460&#160;km) at current payloads. The higher-weight version was offered for introduction to service early in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-delivery_problems">Post-delivery problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Post-delivery problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During repairs following the <a href="/wiki/Qantas_Flight_32" title="Qantas Flight 32">Qantas Flight 32</a> engine failure incident, cracks were discovered in wing fittings. As a result, the <a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">European Aviation Safety Agency</a> issued an <a href="/wiki/Airworthiness_Directive" title="Airworthiness Directive">Airworthiness Directive</a> in January 2012 which affected 20 A380 aircraft that had accumulated over 1,300 flights.<sup id="cite_ref-EASA_Wing_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EASA_Wing-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> A380s with under 1,800 flight hours were to be inspected within 6 weeks or 84 flights; aircraft with over 1,800 flight hours were to be examined within four days or 14 flights.<sup id="cite_ref-AH44992a89_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AH44992a89-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AD_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AD-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Fittings found to be cracked were replaced.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> On 8 February 2012, the checks were extended to cover all 68 A380 aircraft in operation. The problem is considered to be minor and is not expected to affect operations.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC16942361_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC16942361-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> EADS acknowledged that the cost of repairs would be over $130 million, to be borne by Airbus. The company said the problem was traced to stress and material used for the fittings.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, major airlines are seeking compensation from Airbus for revenue lost as a result of the cracks and subsequent grounding of fleets.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Airbus has switched to a different type of aluminium alloy so aircraft delivered from 2014 onwards should not have this problem.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus is changing about 10% of all doors, as some leak during flight. One occurrence resulted in dropped <a href="/wiki/Emergency_oxygen_system" title="Emergency oxygen system">oxygen masks</a> and an emergency landing. The switch is expected to cost over \xe2\x82\xac100 million. Airbus states that safety is sufficient, as the air pressure pushes the door into the frame.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380_cross_section.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Airbus_A380_cross_section.svg/170px-Airbus_A380_cross_section.svg.png" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Airbus_A380_cross_section.svg/255px-Airbus_A380_cross_section.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Airbus_A380_cross_section.svg/340px-Airbus_A380_cross_section.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380_cross_section.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The A380 cabin cross-section with <a href="/wiki/Economy-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Economy-class">economy-class</a> seating</div></div></div>\n<p>The A380 was initially offered in two models: the <i>A380-800</i> and the <i>A380F</i>.\n</p><p>The A380-800\'s original configuration carried 555 passengers in a <a href="/wiki/Travel_class" title="Travel class">three-class</a> configuration<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> or 853 passengers (538 on the main deck and 315 on the upper deck) in a single-class economy configuration. Then in May 2007, Airbus began marketing a configuration with 30 fewer passengers (525 total in three classes)\xe2\x80\x94traded for 200&#160;nmi (370&#160;km) more range\xe2\x80\x94to better reflect trends in premium-class accommodation.<sup id="cite_ref-555_to_525_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-555_to_525-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The design range for the 380\xe2\x88\x92800 model is 8,500&#160;nmi (15,700&#160;km);<sup id="cite_ref-a380_specs_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a380_specs-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> capable of flying from Hong Kong to New York or from Sydney to <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> non-stop.\n</p><p>The second model, the <i>A380F</i> freighter, would carry 150&#160;tonnes of cargo with a range of 5,600&#160;nmi (10,400&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-a380_freighter_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a380_freighter-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The freighter development was put on hold as Airbus prioritised the passenger version, and all cargo orders were cancelled.\n</p><p>Future variants may include an <i>A380-900</i> stretch\xe2\x80\x93seating about 656 passengers (or up to 960 passengers in an all-economy configuration)\xe2\x80\x93and an extended-range version with the same passenger capacity as the A380-800.<sup id="cite_ref-norris_wagner_book_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris_wagner_book-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Engines">Engines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Engines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_Lagard%C3%A8re_-_GP7200_engine_MSN108_(1).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Airbus_Lagard%C3%A8re_-_GP7200_engine_MSN108_%281%29.JPG/220px-Airbus_Lagard%C3%A8re_-_GP7200_engine_MSN108_%281%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Airbus_Lagard%C3%A8re_-_GP7200_engine_MSN108_%281%29.JPG/330px-Airbus_Lagard%C3%A8re_-_GP7200_engine_MSN108_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Airbus_Lagard%C3%A8re_-_GP7200_engine_MSN108_%281%29.JPG/440px-Airbus_Lagard%C3%A8re_-_GP7200_engine_MSN108_%281%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_Lagard%C3%A8re_-_GP7200_engine_MSN108_(1).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Engine_Alliance_GP7200" class="mw-redirect" title="Engine Alliance GP7200">Engine Alliance GP7200</a> engine waiting for installation</div></div></div>\n<p>The A380 is offered with the <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Trent_900" title="Rolls-Royce Trent 900">Rolls-Royce Trent 900</a> (A380-841/-842) or the <a href="/wiki/Engine_Alliance_GP7000" title="Engine Alliance GP7000">Engine Alliance GP7000</a> (A380-861) <a href="/wiki/Turbofan" title="Turbofan">turbofan</a> engines.<sup id="cite_ref-TCDS_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCDS-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\nThe Trent 900 is a combination of the 3&#160;m (118&#160;in) fan and scaled <abbr title="intermediate pressure">IP</abbr> compressor of the 777-200X/300X <a href="/wiki/Trent_8104" class="mw-redirect" title="Trent 8104">Trent 8104</a> technology demonstrator derived from the Boeing 777\'s <a href="/wiki/Trent_800" class="mw-redirect" title="Trent 800">Trent 800</a>, and the Airbus A340-500/600\'s <a href="/wiki/Trent_500" class="mw-redirect" title="Trent 500">Trent 500</a> core.\nThe GP7200 <abbr title="high-pressure">HP</abbr> core technology is derived from GE\'s <a href="/wiki/GE90" class="mw-redirect" title="GE90">GE90</a> and its <abbr title="low-pressure">LP</abbr> sections are based on the <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney_PW4000" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney PW4000">PW4000</a> expertise.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight20may2003_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight20may2003-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\nAt its launch in 2000, engine makers assured Airbus it was getting the best level of technology and they would be state of the art for the next decade, but three years later Boeing launched the 787 with game-changing technology and 10% lower fuel burn than the previous generation, to the dismay of John Leahy.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Thanks to its modern engines and aerodynamic improvements, Lufthansa\'s A380s produce half the noise of the Boeing 747-200 while carrying 160 more passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2012, the A380 received an award from the <a href="/wiki/Noise_Abatement_Society" title="Noise Abatement Society">Noise Abatement Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow</a> is a key destination for the A380.<sup id="cite_ref-norris_wagner_book_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris_wagner_book-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\nThe aircraft is below the QC/2 departure and QC/0.5 arrival noise limits under the <a href="/wiki/Quota_Count_system" title="Quota Count system">Quota Count system</a> set by the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\nField measurements suggest the approach quota allocation for the A380 may be overly generous compared to the older Boeing 747, but still quieter.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\nRolls-Royce is supporting the CAA in understanding the relatively high A380/Trent 900 monitored noise levels.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\nHeathrow\xe2\x80\x99s landing charges having a noise component, the A380 is cheaper to land there than a Boeing 777-200 and -300 and it saves $4,300 to $5,200 per landing, or $15.3M to $18.8M of <a href="/wiki/Present_value" title="Present value">present value</a> over 15 years. <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Narita" class="mw-redirect" title="Tokyo Narita">Tokyo Narita</a> has a similar noise charge.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sufficient braking capacity allowed for <a href="/wiki/Thrust_reverser" class="mw-redirect" title="Thrust reverser">thrust reversers</a> to be installed on only the inboard engines.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\nThe outboard engines lack them, reducing the amount of debris stirred up during landing.<sup id="cite_ref-HuberStop_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HuberStop-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\nThey are electrically actuated to save weight and for better reliability than pneumatic or hydraulic equivalents.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wings">Wings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Wings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/A380_01.jpg/220px-A380_01.jpg" width="220" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/A380_01.jpg/330px-A380_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/A380_01.jpg/440px-A380_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2352" data-file-height="2434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Planform view showing moderate wing aspect ratio and the undercarriage kinematics</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IABG_Test_Setup_A380_Dresden_bent_wing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/IABG_Test_Setup_A380_Dresden_bent_wing.jpg/220px-IABG_Test_Setup_A380_Dresden_bent_wing.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/IABG_Test_Setup_A380_Dresden_bent_wing.jpg/330px-IABG_Test_Setup_A380_Dresden_bent_wing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/IABG_Test_Setup_A380_Dresden_bent_wing.jpg/440px-IABG_Test_Setup_A380_Dresden_bent_wing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="731" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IABG_Test_Setup_A380_Dresden_bent_wing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Composite photo of a structural loading test on the left wing box</div></div></div>\n<p>The A380\'s wing is sized for a <a href="/wiki/Maximum_takeoff_weight" title="Maximum takeoff weight">maximum takeoff weight</a> (MTOW) over 650&#160;tonnes to accommodate these future versions, albeit with some internal strengthening required on the A380F freighter.<sup id="cite_ref-norris_wagner_book_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris_wagner_book-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The optimal wingspan for this weight is about 90&#160;m (300&#160;ft), but airport restrictions limited it to less than 80&#160;m (260&#160;ft), lowering <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio_(aerodynamics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aspect ratio (aerodynamics)">aspect ratio</a> to 7.8 which reduces <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">fuel efficiency</a><sup id="cite_ref-leeUp_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeUp-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> about 10% and increases <a href="/wiki/Operating_cost" title="Operating cost">operating costs</a> a few percent,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> given that fuel costs constitute about 50% of the cost of long-haul airplane operation.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>  The common wing design approach sacrifices fuel efficiency on the A380-800 passenger model because of its weight but Airbus estimates that the aircraft\'s size and advanced technology will provide lower operating costs per passenger than the 747-400. The wings incorporate <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device" title="Wingtip device">wingtip fences</a> that extend above and below the wing surface, similar to those on the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">A310</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">A320</a>. These increase fuel efficiency and range by reducing <a href="/wiki/Lift-induced_drag" title="Lift-induced drag">induced drag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The wingtip fences also reduce <a href="/wiki/Wake_turbulence" title="Wake turbulence">wake turbulence</a>, which endangers following aircraft and could, theoretically, damage house roofs.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Materials">Materials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Materials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>While most of the fuselage is made of aluminium alloys, <a href="/wiki/Composite_materials" class="mw-redirect" title="Composite materials">composite materials</a> comprise more than 20% of the A380\'s <a href="/wiki/Airframe" title="Airframe">airframe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carbon_fibre_reinforced_plastic" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon fibre reinforced plastic">Carbon-fibre reinforced plastic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glass-reinforced_plastic" class="mw-redirect" title="Glass-reinforced plastic">glass-fibre reinforced plastic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quartz-fibre" class="mw-redirect" title="Quartz-fibre">quartz-fibre reinforced plastic</a> are used extensively in wings, fuselage sections (such as the undercarriage and rear end of fuselage), tail surfaces, and doors.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The A380 is the first commercial airliner to have a central wing box made of carbon fibre reinforced plastic. It is also the first to have a smoothly contoured wing cross section. The wings of other commercial airliners are partitioned span-wise into sections. This flowing continuous cross section reduces aerodynamic drag. <a href="/wiki/Thermoplastics" class="mw-redirect" title="Thermoplastics">Thermoplastics</a> are used in the leading edges of the <a href="/wiki/Leading_edge_slats" class="mw-redirect" title="Leading edge slats">slats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The hybrid fibre metal laminate material <a href="/wiki/GLARE" title="GLARE">GLARE</a> (glass laminate aluminium reinforced epoxy) is used in the upper fuselage and on the stabilisers\' leading edges.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> This aluminium-<a href="/wiki/Fibreglass" class="mw-redirect" title="Fibreglass">glass-fibre</a> <a href="/wiki/Laminate" class="mw-redirect" title="Laminate">laminate</a> is lighter and has better corrosion and impact resistance than conventional aluminium <a href="/wiki/Alloys" class="mw-redirect" title="Alloys">alloys</a> used in aviation.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Unlike earlier composite materials, GLARE can be repaired using conventional aluminium repair techniques. The application of GLARE on the A380 has a long history, which shows the complex nature of innovations in the aircraft industry.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Newer <a href="/wiki/Welding" title="Welding">weldable</a> aluminium alloys are used in the A380\'s airframe. This enables the widespread use of <a href="/wiki/Laser_beam_welding" title="Laser beam welding">laser beam welding</a> manufacturing techniques, eliminating rows of <a href="/wiki/Rivet" title="Rivet">rivets</a> and resulting in a lighter, stronger structure.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> High-strength aluminium (type 7449)<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> reinforced with carbon fibre was used in the wing brackets of the first 120 A380s to reduce weight, but cracks have been discovered and new sets of the more critical brackets will be made of standard <a href="/wiki/Aluminium_alloy#Wrought_alloys" title="Aluminium alloy">aluminium 7010</a>, increasing weight by 90&#160;kg (198&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Repair costs for earlier aircraft are expected to be around \xe2\x82\xac500 million (US$629 million).<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It takes 3,600&#160;L (950&#160;US&#160;gal) of paint to cover the 3,100&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (33,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) exterior of an A380.<sup id="cite_ref-A380_Paint_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380_Paint-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The paint is
