five layers thick and weighs about 650&#160;kg (1,433&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Avionics">Avionics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Avionics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The A380 employs an <a href="/wiki/Integrated_modular_avionics" title="Integrated modular avionics">integrated modular avionics</a> (IMA) architecture, first used in advanced military aircraft, such as the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_F-22_Raptor" title="Lockheed Martin F-22 Raptor">Lockheed Martin F-22 Raptor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_F-35_Lightning_II" title="Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II">Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-lessismore_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lessismore-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Rafale" title="Dassault Rafale">Dassault Rafale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> The main IMA systems on the A380 were developed by the <a href="/wiki/Thales_Group" title="Thales Group">Thales Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thales_tech_onboard_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thales_tech_onboard-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Designed and developed by Airbus, Thales and <a href="/wiki/Diehl_Aerospace" title="Diehl Aerospace">Diehl Aerospace</a>, the IMA suite was first used on the A380. The suite is a technological innovation, with networked computing modules to support different applications.<sup id="cite_ref-Thales_tech_onboard_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thales_tech_onboard-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The data networks use <a href="/wiki/Avionics_Full-Duplex_Switched_Ethernet" title="Avionics Full-Duplex Switched Ethernet">Avionics Full-Duplex Switched Ethernet</a>, an implementation of ARINC 664. These are switched, <a href="/wiki/Full-duplex" class="mw-redirect" title="Full-duplex">full-duplex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Star_network" title="Star network">star-topology</a> and based on <a href="/wiki/Ethernet_over_twisted_pair" title="Ethernet over twisted pair">100baseTX</a> <a href="/wiki/Fast_Ethernet" title="Fast Ethernet">fast-Ethernet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> This reduces the amount of wiring required and minimises <a href="/wiki/Latency_(engineering)" title="Latency (engineering)">latency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-avionics_magazine_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avionics_magazine-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380_cockpit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Airbus_A380_cockpit.jpg/220px-Airbus_A380_cockpit.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Airbus_A380_cockpit.jpg/330px-Airbus_A380_cockpit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Airbus_A380_cockpit.jpg/440px-Airbus_A380_cockpit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380_cockpit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A380 flight deck</div></div></div>\n<p>Airbus used similar cockpit layout, procedures and handling characteristics to other Airbus aircraft, reducing crew training costs. The A380 has an improved <a href="/wiki/Glass_cockpit" title="Glass cockpit">glass cockpit</a>, using <a href="/wiki/Fly-by-wire" title="Fly-by-wire">fly-by-wire</a> flight controls linked to <a href="/wiki/Joystick" title="Joystick">side-sticks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Timesindepth_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timesindepth-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The cockpit has eight 15 by 20&#160;cm (5.9 by 7.9&#160;in) <a href="/wiki/Liquid_crystal_display" class="mw-redirect" title="Liquid crystal display">liquid crystal displays</a>, all physically identical and interchangeable; comprising two <a href="/wiki/Primary_flight_display" title="Primary flight display">primary flight displays</a>, two navigation displays, one engine parameter display, one system display and two <a href="/wiki/Multi-function_display" title="Multi-function display">multi-function displays</a>. The MFDs were introduced on the A380 to provide an easy-to-use interface to the <a href="/wiki/Flight_management_system" title="Flight management system">flight management system</a>\xe2\x80\x94replacing three multifunction control and display units.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> They include <a href="/wiki/QWERTY" title="QWERTY">QWERTY</a> keyboards and trackballs, interfacing with a <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">graphical</a> "<a href="/wiki/Point-and-click" class="mw-redirect" title="Point-and-click">point-and-click</a>" display system.<sup id="cite_ref-a380_flight_deck_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a380_flight_deck-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Network Systems Server (NSS) is the heart of A380\'s paperless cockpit; it eliminates bulky manuals and traditional charts.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The NSS has enough inbuilt robustness to eliminate onboard backup paper documents. The A380\'s network and server system stores data and offers electronic documentation, providing a required equipment list, navigation charts, performance calculations, and an aircraft logbook. This is accessed through the MFDs and controlled via the keyboard interface.<sup id="cite_ref-avionics_magazine_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avionics_magazine-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Fly-by-wire#Power-by-wire" title="Fly-by-wire">Power-by-wire</a> flight control actuators have been used for the first time in civil aviation to back up primary <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydraulic">hydraulic</a> actuators. Also, during certain manoeuvres they augment the primary actuators.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> They have self-contained hydraulic and electrical power supplies. Electro-hydrostatic actuators (EHA) are used in the <a href="/wiki/Aileron" title="Aileron">aileron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elevator_(aircraft)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elevator (aircraft)">elevator</a>, electric and hydraulic motors to drive the slats as well as electrical backup hydrostatic actuators (EBHA) for the rudder and some spoilers.<sup id="cite_ref-avionics_magazine2_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avionics_magazine2-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The A380\'s 350&#160;bar (35&#160;MPa or 5,000&#160;psi) hydraulic system is a significant difference from the typical 210&#160;bar (21&#160;MPa or 3,000&#160;psi) hydraulics used on most commercial aircraft since the 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Highlowpress_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highlowpress-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> First used in military aircraft, high-pressure hydraulics reduce the weight and size of pipelines, actuators and related components. The 350&#160;bar pressure is generated by eight de-clutchable hydraulic pumps.<sup id="cite_ref-Highlowpress_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highlowpress-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The hydraulic lines are typically made from <a href="/wiki/Titanium" title="Titanium">titanium</a>; the system features both fuel- and air-cooled <a href="/wiki/Heat_exchanger" title="Heat exchanger">heat exchangers</a>. Self-contained electrically powered hydraulic power packs serve as backups for the primary systems, instead of a secondary hydraulic system, saving weight and reducing maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The A380 uses four 150&#160;kVA variable-frequency electrical generators,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> eliminating constant-speed drives and improving reliability.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The A380 uses aluminium power cables instead of copper for weight reduction. The electrical power system is fully computerised and many <a href="/wiki/Relay#Types" title="Relay">contactors</a> and breakers have been replaced by solid-state devices for better performance and increased reliability.<sup id="cite_ref-avionics_magazine2_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avionics_magazine2-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The auxiliary power comprises the <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_Power_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Auxiliary Power Unit">Auxiliary Power Unit</a> (APU), the electronic control box (ECB), and mounting hardware. The APU in use on the A380 is the PW 980A APU. The APU primarily provides air to power the Analysis Ground Station (AGS) on the ground and to start the engines. The AGS is a semi-automatic analysis system of flight data that helps to optimise management of maintenance and reduce costs. The APU also powers electric generators that provide auxiliary electric power to the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_provisions">Passenger provisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Passenger provisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Seat_configurations_of_Airbus_A380" title="Seat configurations of Airbus A380">Seat configurations of Airbus A380</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380-861,_Emirates_AN1721793.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1721793.jpg/220px-Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1721793.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1721793.jpg/330px-Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1721793.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1721793.jpg/440px-Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1721793.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380-861,_Emirates_AN1721793.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>10 across <a href="/wiki/Economy_class" title="Economy class">economy class</a> seating</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380-861,_Emirates_AN1385446.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1385446.jpg/220px-Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1385446.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1385446.jpg/330px-Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1385446.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1385446.jpg/440px-Airbus_A380-861%2C_Emirates_AN1385446.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380-861,_Emirates_AN1385446.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Emirates <a href="/wiki/Business_class" title="Business class">business class</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Etihad_Airways_aircraft_interiors_demo_ITB_2017_(08).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Etihad_Airways_aircraft_interiors_demo_ITB_2017_%2808%29.JPG/220px-Etihad_Airways_aircraft_interiors_demo_ITB_2017_%2808%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Etihad_Airways_aircraft_interiors_demo_ITB_2017_%2808%29.JPG/330px-Etihad_Airways_aircraft_interiors_demo_ITB_2017_%2808%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Etihad_Airways_aircraft_interiors_demo_ITB_2017_%2808%29.JPG/440px-Etihad_Airways_aircraft_interiors_demo_ITB_2017_%2808%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Etihad_Airways_aircraft_interiors_demo_ITB_2017_(08).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Etihad The Residence Apartment with bedroom, living room and an en-suite shower room on Airbus A380-800</div></div></div>\n<p>The cabin has features to reduce traveller fatigue such as a quieter interior and higher pressurisation than previous generations of aircraft; the A380 is pressurised to the equivalent altitude of 1,520&#160;m (5,000&#160;ft) up to 12,000&#160;m (39,000&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> It has 50% less cabin noise, 50% more cabin area and volume, larger windows, bigger overhead bins, and 60&#160;cm (2.0&#160;ft) extra headroom versus the 747-400.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-a380_figures_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a380_figures-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Seating options range from 3-room 12&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (130&#160;sq&#160;ft) "residence" in first class to 11-across in economy.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> A380 economy seats are up to 48&#160;cm (19&#160;in) wide in a 10-abreast configuration,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> compared with the 10-abreast configuration on the 747-400 that typically has seats 44.5&#160;cm (17.5&#160;in) wide.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> On other aircraft, economy seats range from 41.5 to 52.3&#160;cm (16.3 to 20.6&#160;in) in width.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The A380\'s upper and lower decks are connected by two stairways, <a href="/wiki/Bow_(ship)" title="Bow (ship)">fore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aft" title="Aft">aft</a>, wide enough to accommodate two passengers side-by-side; this cabin arrangement allows multiple seat configurations. The maximum certified carrying capacity is 853 passengers in an all-economy-class layout,<sup id="cite_ref-evacuation_test_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evacuation_test-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Airbus lists the "typical" three-class layout as accommodating 525 passengers, with 10 first, 76 business, and 439 economy class seats.<sup id="cite_ref-555_to_525_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-555_to_525-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Airline configurations range from <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a>\'s 407 passengers to <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>\' two-class 615 seats for <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cpA380_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpA380-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> and average around 480\xe2\x80\x93490 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Air_Austral" title="Air Austral">Air Austral</a>\'s proposed 840 passenger layout has not come to fruition. The A380\'s interior illumination system uses bulbless <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">LEDs</a> in the cabin, cockpit, and cargo decks. The LEDs in the cabin can be altered to create an ambience simulating daylight, night, or intermediate levels.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> On the outside of the aircraft, <a href="/wiki/High-intensity_discharge_lamp" title="High-intensity discharge lamp">HID</a> lighting is used for brighter illumination.\n</p><p>Airbus\'s publicity has stressed the comfort and space of the A380 cabin,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> and advertised onboard relaxation areas such as bars, beauty salons, <a href="/wiki/Duty-free_shop" title="Duty-free shop">duty-free shops</a>, and restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wp_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Proposed amenities resembled those installed on earlier airliners, particularly 1970s wide-body jets,<sup id="cite_ref-fancy_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fancy-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> which largely gave way to regular seats for more passenger capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-fancy_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fancy-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Airbus has acknowledged that some cabin proposals were unlikely to be installed,<sup id="cite_ref-wp_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> and that it was ultimately the airlines\' decision how to configure the interior.<sup id="cite_ref-fancy_218-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fancy-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Industry analysts suggested that implementing customisation has slowed the production speeds, and raised costs.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Due to delivery delays, Singapore Airlines and Air France debuted their seat designs on different aircraft prior to the A380.<sup id="cite_ref-sqcabin_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sqcabin-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prem_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prem-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_Airbus_A380-861_onboard_bar_Iwelumo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Emirates_Airbus_A380-861_onboard_bar_Iwelumo.jpg/220px-Emirates_Airbus_A380-861_onboard_bar_Iwelumo.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Emirates_Airbus_A380-861_onboard_bar_Iwelumo.jpg/330px-Emirates_Airbus_A380-861_onboard_bar_Iwelumo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Emirates_Airbus_A380-861_onboard_bar_Iwelumo.jpg/440px-Emirates_Airbus_A380-861_onboard_bar_Iwelumo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="733" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_Airbus_A380-861_onboard_bar_Iwelumo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bar on an Emirates A380</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_A380_Shower_SPA_ITB2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Emirates_A380_Shower_SPA_ITB2014.jpg/220px-Emirates_A380_Shower_SPA_ITB2014.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Emirates_A380_Shower_SPA_ITB2014.jpg/330px-Emirates_A380_Shower_SPA_ITB2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Emirates_A380_Shower_SPA_ITB2014.jpg/440px-Emirates_A380_Shower_SPA_ITB2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_A380_Shower_SPA_ITB2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Emirates first class shower</div></div></div>\n<p>Initial operators typically configured their A380s for three-class service, while adding extra features for passengers in premium cabins. Launch customer Singapore Airlines introduced partly enclosed first class suites on its A380s in 2007, each featuring a leather seat with a separate bed; center suites could be joined to create a double bed.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SQsuite_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SQsuite-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> A year later, Qantas debuted a new first class <a href="/wiki/Airline_seat#Lie_flat/flat_bed_seating" title="Airline seat">seat-bed</a> and a sofa lounge at the front of the upper deck on its A380s,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> and in 2009 Air France unveiled an upper deck electronic art gallery.<sup id="cite_ref-comp_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comp-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> In late 2008, Emirates introduced "shower spas" in first class on its A380s allowing each first class passenger five minutes of hot water,<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-timesonline_firstlook_emirates_a380_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline_firstlook_emirates_a380-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> drawing on 2.5 tonnes of water although only 60% of it was used.<sup id="cite_ref-fgLook_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fgLook-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Emirates,<sup id="cite_ref-emirates_first_class_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emirates_first_class-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asia_travel_tips_emirates_a380_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asia_travel_tips_emirates_a380-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Etihad Airways and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> also have a bar lounge and seating area on the upper deck, while Etihad has enclosed areas for two people each.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> In addition to lounge areas, some A380 operators have installed amenities consistent with other aircraft in their respective fleets, including self-serve snack bars,<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Premium_economy" title="Premium economy">premium economy</a> sections,<sup id="cite_ref-prem_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prem-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> and redesigned business class seating.<sup id="cite_ref-sqcabin_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sqcabin-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Hamburg Aircraft Interiors Expo in April 2015 saw the presentation of an 11-seat row economy cabin for the A380.  Airbus is reacting to a changing economy; the recession which began in 2008 saw a drop in market percentage of first class and business seats to six percent and an increase in budget economy travelers. Among other causes is the reluctance of employers to pay for executives to travel in First or Business Class. Airbus\' chief of cabin marketing, Ingo Wuggestzer, told Aviation Week and Space Technology that the standard three class cabin no longer reflected market conditions. The 11 seat row on the A380 is accompanied by similar options on other widebodies: nine across on the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a> and ten across on the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350">A350</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Integration_with_infrastructure_and_regulations">Integration with infrastructure and regulations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Integration with infrastructure and regulations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_operations">Ground operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ground operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Qatar_Airways_Airbus_A380-800_at_Heathrow_Airport_Terminal_4_before_Flying_to_Doha,_6_Jan_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Qatar_Airways_Airbus_A380-800_at_Heathrow_Airport_Terminal_4_before_Flying_to_Doha%2C_6_Jan_2015.jpg/220px-Qatar_Airways_Airbus_A380-800_at_Heathrow_Airport_Terminal_4_before_Flying_to_Doha%2C_6_Jan_2015.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Qatar_Airways_Airbus_A380-800_at_Heathrow_Airport_Terminal_4_before_Flying_to_Doha%2C_6_Jan_2015.jpg/330px-Qatar_Airways_Airbus_A380-800_at_Heathrow_Airport_Terminal_4_before_Flying_to_Doha%2C_6_Jan_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Qatar_Airways_Airbus_A380-800_at_Heathrow_Airport_Terminal_4_before_Flying_to_Doha%2C_6_Jan_2015.jpg/440px-Qatar_Airways_Airbus_A380-800_at_Heathrow_Airport_Terminal_4_before_Flying_to_Doha%2C_6_Jan_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Qatar_Airways_Airbus_A380-800_at_Heathrow_Airport_Terminal_4_before_Flying_to_Doha,_6_Jan_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Aircraft_ground_handling" title="Aircraft ground handling">Aircraft ground handling</a> with separate <a href="/wiki/Jetway" class="mw-redirect" title="Jetway">jetways</a> for the main and upper deck, and <a href="/wiki/Ground_support_equipment" title="Ground support equipment">ground support equipment</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In the 1990s, aircraft manufacturers were planning to introduce larger planes than the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a>. In a common effort of the <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization" title="International Civil Aviation Organization">International Civil Aviation Organization</a> (ICAO) with manufacturers, airports and its member agencies, the "80-metre box" was created, the <a href="/wiki/Gate_(airport)" title="Gate (airport)">airport gates</a> allowing planes up to 80&#160;m (260&#160;ft) wingspan and length to be accommodated.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Airbus designed the A380 according to these guidelines,<sup id="cite_ref-ACAP_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACAP-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> and to operate safely on Group V runways and taxiways with a 60 metres (200&#160;ft) loadbearing width.<sup id="cite_ref-ecac_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecac-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> The US FAA initially opposed this,<sup id="cite_ref-faa_eb65_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faa_eb65-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-faa_eb63a_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faa_eb63a-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> then in July 2007, the FAA and EASA agreed to let the A380 operate on 45&#160;m (148&#160;ft) runways without restrictions.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> The A380-800 is approximately 30% larger in overall size than the 747-400.<sup id="cite_ref-usdebut_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usdebut-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-awpilot_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awpilot-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Runway lighting and signage may need changes to provide clearance to the wings and avoid blast damage from the engines. Runways, runway shoulders and taxiway shoulders may be required to be stabilised to reduce the likelihood of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_object_damage" title="Foreign object damage">foreign object damage</a> caused to (or by) the outboard engines, which are more than 25&#160;m (82&#160;ft) from the centre line of the aircraft,<sup id="cite_ref-ACAP_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACAP-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ecac_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecac-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Airports_Prepare_for_the_A380_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airports_Prepare_for_the_A380-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> compared to 21&#160;m (69&#160;ft) for the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">747\xe2\x80\x93400</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-747_airport_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-747_airport-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8" title="Boeing 747-8">747\xe2\x80\x938</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-747-8_airport_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-747-8_airport-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380_Fahrwerk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Airbus_A380_Fahrwerk.jpg/220px-Airbus_A380_Fahrwerk.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Airbus_A380_Fahrwerk.jpg/330px-Airbus_A380_Fahrwerk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Airbus_A380_Fahrwerk.jpg/440px-Airbus_A380_Fahrwerk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380_Fahrwerk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A380 20-wheel main <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Airbus measured pavement loads using a 540-tonne (595&#160;short tons) ballasted test rig, designed to replicate the <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a> of the A380. The rig was towed over a section of pavement at Airbus\' facilities that had been instrumented with embedded load sensors.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> It was determined that the pavement of most runways will not need to be reinforced despite the higher weight,<sup id="cite_ref-Airports_Prepare_for_the_A380_244-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airports_Prepare_for_the_A380-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> as it is distributed on more wheels than in other passenger aircraft with a total of 22 wheels (that is, its <a href="/wiki/Ground_pressure" title="Ground pressure">ground pressure</a> is lower).<sup id="cite_ref-test_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> The A380 undercarriage consists of four main landing gear legs and one noseleg (a similar layout to the 747), with the two inboard landing gear legs each supporting six wheels.<sup id="cite_ref-test_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The A380 requires service vehicles with lifts capable of reaching the upper deck,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Pushback" title="Pushback">tractors</a> capable of handling the A380\'s maximum ramp weight.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> When using two jetway bridges the boarding time is 45 min, and when using an extra jetway to the upper deck it is reduced to 34 min.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> The A380 has an airport turnaround time of 90\xe2\x80\x93110 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-fgLook_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fgLook-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In 2008 the A380 test aircraft were used to trial the modifications made to several airports to accommodate the type.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Takeoff_and_landing_separation">Takeoff and landing separation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Takeoff and landing separation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A6-ADT_A380_Emirates_(8557113059).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/A6-ADT_A380_Emirates_%288557113059%29.jpg/220px-A6-ADT_A380_Emirates_%288557113059%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/A6-ADT_A380_Emirates_%288557113059%29.jpg/330px-A6-ADT_A380_Emirates_%288557113059%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/A6-ADT_A380_Emirates_%288557113059%29.jpg/440px-A6-ADT_A380_Emirates_%288557113059%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1267" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A6-ADT_A380_Emirates_(8557113059).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wingtip_vortex" class="mw-redirect" title="Wingtip vortex">Wingtip vortex</a> left behind</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2005, the ICAO recommended that provisional separation criteria for the A380 on takeoff<sup id="cite_ref-Daniel_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daniel-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> and landing be substantially greater than for the 747 because preliminary <a href="/wiki/Flight_test" title="Flight test">flight test</a> data suggested a stronger <a href="/wiki/Wake_turbulence" title="Wake turbulence">wake turbulence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> These criteria were in effect while the ICAO\'s wake vortex steering group, with representatives from the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Aviation_Authorities" title="Joint Aviation Authorities">JAA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a>, the FAA, and Airbus, refined its 3-year study of the issue with additional <a href="/wiki/Flight_testing" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight testing">flight testing</a>. In September 2006, the working group presented its first conclusions to the ICAO.<sup id="cite_ref-vortex_study_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vortex_study-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2006, the ICAO issued new interim recommendations. Replacing a blanket 10 nautical miles (19&#160;km) separation for aircraft trailing an A380 during approach, the new distances were 6&#160;nmi (11&#160;km), 8&#160;nmi (15&#160;km) and 10&#160;nmi (19&#160;km) respectively for non-A380 "Heavy", "Medium", and "Light" ICAO aircraft categories. These compared with the 4&#160;nmi (7.4&#160;km), 5&#160;nmi (9.3&#160;km) and 6&#160;nmi (11&#160;km) spacing applicable to other "Heavy" aircraft. Another A380 following an A380 should maintain a separation of 4&#160;nmi (7.4&#160;km). On departure behind an A380, non-A380 "Heavy" aircraft are required to wait two minutes, and "Medium"/"Light" aircraft three minutes for time based operations. The ICAO also recommends that pilots append the term "Super" to the aircraft\'s callsign when initiating communication with air traffic control, to distinguish the A380 from "Heavy" aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-icao_wake_guidance_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icao_wake_guidance-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2008, the ICAO issued revised approach separations of 4&#160;nmi (7.4&#160;km) for Super (another A380), 6&#160;nmi (11&#160;km) for Heavy, 7&#160;nmi (13&#160;km) for medium/small, and 8&#160;nmi (15&#160;km) for light.<sup id="cite_ref-FG_2008_sep_distances_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG_2008_sep_distances-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> In November 2008, an incident on a parallel runway during crosswinds made the Australian authorities change procedures for those conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Singapore Airlines describe the A380\'s landing speed of 130\xe2\x80\x93135&#160;kn (240\xe2\x80\x93250&#160;km/h) as "impressively slow".<sup id="cite_ref-fgPilotRep_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fgPilotRep-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Maintenance">Maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As the A380 fleet grows older, <a href="/wiki/National_Airworthiness_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="National Airworthiness Authority">airworthiness authority</a> rules require certain scheduled <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_maintenance" title="Aircraft maintenance">inspections</a> from approved <a href="/wiki/Maintenance,_repair,_and_operations" class="mw-redirect" title="Maintenance, repair, and operations">aircraft tool shops</a>. The increasing fleet size (to about 286 in 2020) cause expected maintenance and modification to cost $6.8 billion for 2015\xe2\x80\x932020, of which $2.1 billion are for engines.  Emirates performed its first <a href="/wiki/3C_check" class="mw-redirect" title="3C check">3C-check</a> for 55 days in 2014. During lengthy shop stays, some airlines will use the opportunity to install new interiors.<sup id="cite_ref-aw2015-02-02_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aw2015-02-02-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Variants">Variants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Variants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380_on_MAKS_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Airbus_A380_on_MAKS_2011.jpg/220px-Airbus_A380_on_MAKS_2011.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Airbus_A380_on_MAKS_2011.jpg/330px-Airbus_A380_on_MAKS_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Airbus_A380_on_MAKS_2011.jpg/440px-Airbus_A380_on_MAKS_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1156" data-file-height="771" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A380_on_MAKS_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airbus A380 at <a href="/wiki/MAKS_(air_show)" title="MAKS (air show)">MAKS</a> 2011, Russia</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A380F">A380F</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: A380F">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Airbus originally accepted orders for the freighter variant, offering the largest payload capacity of any <a href="/wiki/Cargo_aircraft" title="Cargo aircraft">cargo aircraft</a> in production, exceeded only by the single <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-225_Mriya" title="Antonov An-225 Mriya">Antonov An-225 <i>Mriya</i></a> in service.<sup id="cite_ref-a380f_specs_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a380f_specs-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> An aerospace consultant has estimated that the A380F would have 7% better payload and better range than the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8F" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-8F">Boeing 747-8F</a>, but also higher trip costs.<sup id="cite_ref-and_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-and-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> However, production was suspended until the A380 production lines have settled, with no firm availability date.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fedex_cancel_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fedex_cancel-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Airbus removed A380F from the range of freighters on its corporate website.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> The maximum payload would have been 150&#160;t (330,000&#160;lb), with a 5,600&#160;nmi (10,400&#160;km) range.<sup id="cite_ref-a380_freighter_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a380_freighter-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A patent for "combi" version was applied for. This version would offer the flexibility of carrying both passengers and cargo, along with being rapidly reconfigurable to expand or contract the cargo area and passenger area as needed for a given flight.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A380-900">A380-900</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: A380-900">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In November 2007, Airbus top sales executive and chief operating officer <a href="/wiki/John_Leahy_(executive)" title="John Leahy (executive)">John Leahy</a> confirmed plans for an enlarged variant\xe2\x80\x94the A380-900\xe2\x80\x94with more seating space than the A380-800.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> The A380-900 would have a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> for 650 passengers in standard configuration and for approximately 900 passengers in an economy-only configuration.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> Airlines that expressed an interest in the 380-900 included Emirates,<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> Virgin Atlantic,<sup id="cite_ref-Sea_times-900_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sea_times-900-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Cathay Pacific,<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Air France, KLM, Lufthansa,<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kingfisher_Airlines" title="Kingfisher Airlines">Kingfisher Airlines</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> and leasing company <a href="/wiki/ILFC" class="mw-redirect" title="ILFC">ILFC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> In May 2010, Airbus announced that A380-900 development would be postponed until production of the A380-800 stabilised.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 December 2014, at the annual Airbus Investor Day forum, Airbus CEO controversially announced,  "We will one day launch an A380neo and one day launch a stretched A380".<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> This statement followed speculation sparked by Airbus <a href="/wiki/Chief_financial_officer" title="Chief financial officer">CFO</a> Harald Wilhelm that Airbus could possibly axe the A380 ahead of its time due to softening demand.<sup id="cite_ref-orders-vanish_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orders-vanish-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 June 2015, John Leahy, Airbus\'s chief operating officer for customers, stated that Airbus was again looking at the A380-900 programme. Airbus\'s newest concept would be a stretch of the A380-800 offering 50 seats more\xe2\x80\x94not 100 seats as originally envisaged. This stretch would be tied to a potential re-engining of the A380-800. According to Flight Global, an A380-900 would make better use of the A380\'s existing wing.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A380neo">A380neo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: A380neo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 15 June 2015, Reuters reported that Airbus was discussing a stretched version of the A380 with a half dozen customers.  This aircraft, which could also feature new engines, would accommodate an additional fifty passengers.  Deliveries to customers were planned for sometime in 2020 or 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>  On 19 July 2015, Airbus CEO <a href="/wiki/Fabrice_Br%C3%A9gier" title="Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier">Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier</a> stated that the company will build a new version of the A380 featuring new improved wings and new engines.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> Speculation about the development of a so-called A380neo ("neo" for "new engine option") had been going on for a few months after earlier press releases in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> and in 2015 the company was considering whether to end production of the type prior to 2018<sup id="cite_ref-orders-vanish_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orders-vanish-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> or develop a new A380 variant. Later it was revealed that Airbus was looking at both the possibility of a longer A380 in line of the previously planned A380-900<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> and a new engine version, i.e. A380neo.  Br\xc3\xa9gier also revealed that the new variant would be ready to enter service by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> The engine would most likely be one of a variety of all-new options from Rolls-Royce, ranging from derivatives of the A350\'s XWB-84/97 to the future Advance project due at around 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 June 2016, Emirates President Tim Clark stated that talks between Emirates and Airbus on the A380neo have "lapsed".<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup>  On 12 June 2017, Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier confirmed that Airbus will not launch an A380neo, stating "...there is no business case to do that, this is absolutely clear." However, Br\xc3\xa9gier stated it won\'t stop Airbus from looking at what could be done to improve the performance of the aircraft. One such proposal is a 32&#160;ft (9.8&#160;m) wingspan extension to reduce drag and increase fuel efficiency by 4%,<sup id="cite_ref-winglets-bigger-wing-span_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winglets-bigger-wing-span-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> though further increase is likely to be seen on the aircraft with new <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device#Blended_winglets" title="Wingtip device">Sharklets</a> like on the A380 Plus.<sup id="cite_ref-winglets-bigger-wing-span_288-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winglets-bigger-wing-span-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A380plus">A380plus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: A380plus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_A380plus_winglet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_A380plus_winglet.jpg/220px-Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_A380plus_winglet.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_A380plus_winglet.jpg/330px-Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_A380plus_winglet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_A380plus_winglet.jpg/440px-Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_A380plus_winglet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_A380plus_winglet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The A380plus winglet mockup</div></div></div>\n<p>Launched at the June 2017 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">Paris Air Show</a>, Airbus offers an A380plus enhanced version with 13% lower costs per seat, featuring up to 80 more seats through better use of cabin space, split scimitar <a href="/wiki/Winglet" class="mw-redirect" title="Winglet">winglets</a> and wing refinements allowing a 4% <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_aircraft" title="Fuel economy in aircraft">fuel economy</a> improvement, and longer <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_maintenance" title="Aircraft maintenance">aircraft maintenance</a> intervals with less downtime.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>  Its <a href="/wiki/Maximum_takeoff_weight" title="Maximum takeoff weight">maximum takeoff weight</a> is increased by 3&#160;t (6,600&#160;lb) to 578&#160;t (1,274,000&#160;lb), allowing it to carry more passengers over the same 8,200 nmi range or increase the range by 300&#160;nm. <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> could order 20 aircraft at the November <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Air_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubai Air Show">Dubai Air Show</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The upgrade will be available from 2020.  Winglet mockups, 4.7m (15\xc2\xbdft) high, were displayed on the MSN04 test aircraft at Le Bourget. <a href="/wiki/Wing_twist" title="Wing twist">Wing twist</a> will be modified and <a href="/wiki/Camber_(aerodynamics)" title="Camber (aerodynamics)">camber</a> changed by increasing its height by 33&#160;mm (1.3&#160;in) between Rib 10 and Rib 30, along with upper-belly fairing improvements.  The <a href="/wiki/In-flight_entertainment" title="In-flight entertainment">in-flight entertainment</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Flight_management_system" title="Flight management system">flight management system</a> and the fuel pumps will come from the <a href="/wiki/A350" class="mw-redirect" title="A350">A350</a> to reduce weight and improve reliability and fuel economy. Light checks will be required after 1,000 hr instead of 750 hr and heavy check <a href="/wiki/Downtime" title="Downtime">downtime</a> will be reduced to keep the aircraft flying for six days more per year.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek19June2017_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek19June2017-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Market">Market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_at_Heathrow_(9308336110).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/A380_at_Heathrow_%289308336110%29.jpg/220px-A380_at_Heathrow_%289308336110%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/A380_at_Heathrow_%289308336110%29.jpg/330px-A380_at_Heathrow_%289308336110%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/A380_at_Heathrow_%289308336110%29.jpg/440px-A380_at_Heathrow_%289308336110%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1194" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A380_at_Heathrow_(9308336110).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">Qantas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> Airbus A380s parked at <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Size">Size</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Size">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In its 2000 Global Market Forecast, Airbus estimated the demand for 1,235 passenger Very Large Aircraft (VLA), with more than 400 seats&#160;: 360 up to 2009 and 875 by 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight19sep2017_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight19sep2017-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> The market is estimated for two decades at more than 1,700 by Airbus and 700 by Boeing since 1999-2000, including freighters.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, industry analysts Philip Lawrence of the Aerospace Research Centre in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a> anticipated 880 sales by 2025 with Airbus having conducted the most extensive and thorough market analysis of commercial aviation ever undertaken, justifying its VLA plans to design the A380 by the <a href="/wiki/Spoke-hub_distribution_paradigm" class="mw-redirect" title="Spoke-hub distribution paradigm">spoke-hub distribution paradigm</a> while <a href="/wiki/Richard_Aboulafia" title="Richard Aboulafia">Richard Aboulafia</a> of the consulting Teal Group in <a href="/wiki/Fairfax,_Virginia" title="Fairfax, Virginia">Fairfax, Virginia</a> anticipated 400 with the rise of mid-size aircraft and market fragmentation reducing them to <a href="/wiki/Niche_market" title="Niche market">niche markets</a>, making such plans unjustified in a <a href="/wiki/Point-to-point_transit" title="Point-to-point transit">point-to-point transit</a> model.<sup id="cite_ref-ms_a380_debate_20060905_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ms_a380_debate_20060905-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, Airbus estimated a demand for 1,283 VLA in the following 20 years if airport congestion remains constant, up to 1,771 VLAs if congestion increases, with most deliveries (56%) in Asia-Pacific, and 415 very large, 120-tonne plus freighters.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> For the same period, Boeing was estimating the demand for 590 large (B747 or A380) passenger airliners and 630 freighters.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 May 2018, in its <a href="/wiki/Competition_between_Airbus_and_Boeing#World_Trade_Organization_litigation" title="Competition between Airbus and Boeing">EU appeal ruling</a>, the WTO concluded that the <a href="/wiki/A380" class="mw-redirect" title="A380">A380</a> received improper <a href="/wiki/Subsidies" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsidies">subsidies</a> through $9 billion of launch aids, but Airbus acknowledges that the threat posed to Boeing by the A380 is so marginal with 330 orders since its 2000 launch that any U.S. sanctions should be minimal, as previous rulings showed Boeing\xe2\x80\x99s exposure could be as little as $377 million.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequency_and_capacity">Frequency and capacity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Frequency and capacity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:China_Southern_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Zhao-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/China_Southern_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Zhao-1.jpg/220px-China_Southern_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Zhao-1.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/China_Southern_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Zhao-1.jpg/330px-China_Southern_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Zhao-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/China_Southern_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Zhao-1.jpg/440px-China_Southern_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Zhao-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="824" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:China_Southern_Airlines_Airbus_A380_Zhao-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/China_Southern" class="mw-redirect" title="China Southern">China Southern</a> A380 taking off from <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing Capital Airport">Beijing Capital Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> needed to balance frequency and capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/China_Southern" class="mw-redirect" title="China Southern">China Southern</a> struggled for two years to use its A380s from Beijing, and finally received Boeing 787s in its base in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>, but where it cannot command a premium, unlike Beijing or Shanghai.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Air France withdrew A380 services to Singapore and Montreal and switched to smaller aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, British Airways replaced three 777 flights between London and Los Angeles with two A380 per day.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> Emirates\' <a href="/wiki/Tim_Clark_(airline_executive)" title="Tim Clark (airline executive)">Tim Clark</a> saw a large potential for Asian A380-users, and criticised Airbus\' marketing efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup>  As business travellers prefer more choices offered by more frequencies, flying a route multiple times on smaller aircraft rather than once on a large plane, United Airlines observed the A380 "just doesn\'t really work for us" as it relies on <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787">Boeing 787s</a> operating at a lower trip cost.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the A380 launch, most Europe-Asia and transpacific routes used 747-400s at fairly low frequencies, but since then, routes proliferated with <a href="/wiki/Open_skies" title="Open skies">open skies</a> and most airlines downsized to offer higher frequencies and more routes.\nThe huge capacity offered by each flight eroded the yield: North America was viewed as 17% of the market but it never materialised as a 747 replacement with only fifteen 747s remaining in passenger service in November 2017, for transpacific routes where timezones restrict potential frequency, consolidation changed the networks and US majors constrained capacity and emphasised daily frequencies for business traffic with midsize widebodies like the 787 to extract higher yields, focusing on profits rather than market share leaved to Asian carriers.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight19sep2017_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight19sep2017-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 747 was removed from the <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_flight" title="Transatlantic flight">transatlantic flights</a> by the 767 and from the transpacific market by the 777: newer, smaller aircraft with similar <a href="/wiki/Available_seat_miles" title="Available seat miles">seat-mile</a> costs have lower trip costs and allow more direct routes.\nCabin densification to lower unit costs could aggravate this overcapacity.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight19sep2017_292-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight19sep2017-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_2">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2005, 270 sales were necessary to attain <a href="/wiki/Break-even" title="Break-even">break-even</a> and with 751 expected deliveries its <a href="/wiki/Internal_rate_of_return" title="Internal rate of return">Internal rate of return</a> outlook was at 19%, but due to disruptions in the <a href="/wiki/Ramp-up" title="Ramp-up">ramp-up</a> leading to overcosts and delayed deliveries, it increased to 420 in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, EADS CFO Hans Peter Ring said that break-even could be achieved by 2015 when 200 deliveries were projected.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Airbus clarified that the aircraft production costs would be less than its sales price.<sup id="cite_ref-wsjDMcc_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsjDMcc-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 December 2014, Airbus <a href="/wiki/Chief_financial_officer" title="Chief financial officer">chief financial officer</a> Harald Wilhelm hinted the possibility of ending the programme in 2018, disappointing Emirates president Tim Clark.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> Airbus shares fell down consequently.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup>  Airbus responded to the protests by playing down the possibility the A380 would be abandoned, instead emphasising that enhancing the airplane was a likelier scenario.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> On 22 December 2014, as the jet was about to break even, Airbus CEO <a href="/wiki/Fabrice_Br%C3%A9gier" title="Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier">Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier</a> ruled out cancelling it.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ten years after its first flight, Br\xc3\xa9gier said it was "almost certainly introduced ten years too early".<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> While no longer losing money on each plane sold, Airbus admits that the company will never recoup the $25 billion investment it made in the project.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airbus consistently forecast 1,400 VLA demand over 20-year, still in 2017, and aimed to secure a 50% share, up to 700 units, but delivered \n215 aircraft in 10 years, achieving three produced per month but not the four per month target after the ramp-up to achieve more than 350 and is now declining to 0.5 a month.\nAs Boeing see the VLA market as too small to retain in its 2017 forecast, its VP marketing Randy Tinseth doesn\'t believe Airbus will deliver the rest of the backlog.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight19sep2017_292-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight19sep2017-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Richard Aboulafia predicts a 2020 final delivery, with unpleasant losses due to "hubris, shoddy market analysis, nationalism and simple wishful thinking".\nIn 2017, the A380 fleet overtook the passengers B747s, declining from 740 aircraft when the A380 was launched in 2000 to 550 units at the A380 introduction in 2007, and around 200 ten years after while the combined fleet of A380s and 747s passenger jumbos is 430, the market-share battle having shifted to large single-aisles and 300-seat twin-aisles.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight19sep2017_292-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight19sep2017-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost">Cost</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cost">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the list price of an A380 is US$432.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_prices_first_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_prices_first-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> Negotiated discounts made the actual prices much lower, and industry experts questioned whether the A380 project would ever pay for itself.<sup id="cite_ref-wsjDMcc_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsjDMcc-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The first aircraft was sold and leased back by <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> in 2007 to <a href="/wiki/Dr._Peters" title="Dr. Peters">Dr. Peters</a> for $197 million.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2016, <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">IAG</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Willie_Walsh_(Irish_businessman)" class="mw-redirect" title="Willie Walsh (Irish businessman)">Willie Walsh</a> said he could add a few, but also that he found the price of new aircraft "outrageous" and would source them from the second-hand market.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight19sep2017_292-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight19sep2017-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>AirInsight estimates its hourly cost at $26,000, or around $50 per seat hour (for 520 seats), which compares to $44 per seat hour for a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-300ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-300ER">Boeing 777-300ER</a>, and $90 per seat hour for a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> as of November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup>\nAs it has very large wing and tail surfaces to allow a stretch and a high empty weight per seat, its cost-per-seat advantage eroded, and the <a href="/wiki/A350-1000" class="mw-redirect" title="A350-1000">A350-1000</a> and <a href="/wiki/777-9" class="mw-redirect" title="777-9">777-9</a> will match it.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight19sep2017_292-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight19sep2017-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary">Secondary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Secondary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EGLF_-_Airbus_A380_-_Hifly_-_9H-MIP_(42815400504).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/EGLF_-_Airbus_A380_-_Hifly_-_9H-MIP_%2842815400504%29.jpg/220px-EGLF_-_Airbus_A380_-_Hifly_-_9H-MIP_%2842815400504%29.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/EGLF_-_Airbus_A380_-_Hifly_-_9H-MIP_%2842815400504%29.jpg/330px-EGLF_-_Airbus_A380_-_Hifly_-_9H-MIP_%2842815400504%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/EGLF_-_Airbus_A380_-_Hifly_-_9H-MIP_%2842815400504%29.jpg/440px-EGLF_-_Airbus_A380_-_Hifly_-_9H-MIP_%2842815400504%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4651" data-file-height="3034" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EGLF_-_Airbus_A380_-_Hifly_-_9H-MIP_(42815400504).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hi_Fly_(airline)" title="Hi Fly (airline)">Hi Fly</a> A380 at the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Farnborough_Airshow" title="Farnborough Airshow">Farnborough Airshow</a></div></div></div>\n<p>As of mid-2015, several airlines have expressed their interest in selling their aircraft, partially coinciding with expiring lease contracts for the aircraft. Several A380s which are in service have been offered for lease to other airlines. The suggestion has prompted concerns on the potential for new sales for Airbus, although these were dismissed by Airbus COO John Leahy who stated that "Used A380s do not compete with new A380s", stating that the second-hand market is more interesting for parties otherwise looking to buy smaller aircraft such as the Boeing 777.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines" title="Malaysia Airlines">Malaysia Airlines</a> (MAS) was unable to sell or lease its six A380s, it decided to refurbish the aircraft with seating for 700 and transfer them to a subsidiary carrier for religious <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a> flights.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> As it started receiving its six <a href="/wiki/A350" class="mw-redirect" title="A350">A350s</a> to replace its A380s in December 2017, the new subsidiary will serve the <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Umrah</a> market with them, starting in the third quarter of 2018 and could be expanded above six beyond 2020 to 2022. The cabin will have 36 business seats and 600 economy seats, with a 712-seat reconfiguration possible within five days. The fleet could be <a href="/wiki/Air_charter" title="Air charter">chartered</a> half the year for the <a href="/wiki/Tourism_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourism industry">tourism industry</a> like <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise shipping</a> and will be able to operate for the next 40 years if <a href="/wiki/Oil_price" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil price">oil prices</a> stay low.<sup id="cite_ref-ATW5Jun2017C_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATW5Jun2017C-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup>\nAs they should be parked by June 2018 before reconfiguration, MAS confirmed the plans and will also use them for peak periods to high traffic markets like London.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2017, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Hi_Fly_(airline)" title="Hi Fly (airline)">Hi Fly</a> would lease two used aircraft. The Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Aircraft,_Crew,_Maintenance_and_Insurance" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircraft, Crew, Maintenance and Insurance">ACMI</a>/charter airline will use the aircraft for markets where high capacity is needed and airports where slots are scarce. The first aircraft was scheduled to begin commercial operations during the first quarter of 2018<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> \nHi Fly was to receive its A380s from mid-2018 in a 471-seat configuration: 399 on the main deck, 60 business-class and 12 first-class seats on the upper deck, the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> layout.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup>\nHi Fly first used one of their A380s on 1 August 2018 for a one-off flight to enable <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Airlines" title="Thomas Cook Airlines">Thomas Cook Airlines</a> to repatriate passengers from <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_International_Airport" title="Rhodes International Airport">Rhodes</a> to <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen</a> following IT problems in the Greek airport.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> The same aircraft was then wet-leased to <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian</a> to operate its evening London-New York service for several weeks in August 2018, to alleviate availability issues on its <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787">Boeing 787s</a> affected by <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Trent_1000" title="Rolls-Royce Trent 1000">Trent 1000</a> engine problems;<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> Air Austral also signed a deal to wet-lease an A380 from Hi Fly while one of its 787s is grounded for three months of Trent 1000 inspections.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amedeo_(aircraft_lessor)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Amedeo (aircraft lessor) (page does not exist)">Amedeo</a>, mainly an A380 <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_lessor" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircraft lessor">lessor</a> and the largest with 22, mostly leased to Emirates, wants to find a use for them after their lease expires from 2022, and study if there is a demand to <a href="/wiki/Wet_lease" class="mw-redirect" title="Wet lease">wet lease</a> them.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>\nSwiss aircraft broker <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sparfell_%26_Partners&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sparfell &amp; Partners (page does not exist)">Sparfell &amp; Partners</a> plans to convert for <a href="/wiki/Air_transports_of_heads_of_state_and_government" title="Air transports of heads of state and government">head-of-state</a> or <a href="/wiki/Business_jet" title="Business jet">VVIP transport</a> some of Dr. Peters\' four ex-SIA A380s for under $300 million apiece, less than a new <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Business_Jet" title="Boeing Business Jet">Boeing 777</a> or <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Corporate_Jet" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus Corporate Jet">Airbus A330</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teardown">Teardown</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Teardown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With four A380s leased to Singapore Airlines having been returned between October 2017 and March 2018, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Peters" title="Dr. Peters">Dr. Peters</a> fears a weak <a href="/wiki/Aftermarket_(merchandise)" title="Aftermarket (merchandise)">aftermarket</a> and is considering <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_boneyard" title="Aircraft boneyard">scrapping</a> them, although they are on sale for a <a href="/wiki/Business_jet" title="Business jet">business jet</a> conversion, but on the other hand Airbus sees a potential for <a href="/wiki/African_airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="African airlines">African airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese airlines">Chinese airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> charters and its large Gulf operators.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup>\nAn A380 parted out may be worth $30 million to $50 million if it is at half-life.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Product_teardown" title="Product teardown">Teardown</a> specialists have declined offers for several aircraft at <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_recycling" title="Aircraft recycling">part-out</a> prices due to high risk as a <a href="/wiki/Second-hand" class="mw-redirect" title="Second-hand">secondary market</a> is uncertain with $30 to $40 million for the <a href="/wiki/Remanufacturing" title="Remanufacturing">refurbishment</a>, but should be between $20 to $30 million to be viable.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After proposing the aircraft to <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">BA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hi_Fly_(airline)" title="Hi Fly (airline)">Hi Fly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran_Air" title="Iran Air">Iran Air</a>, Dr. Peters was to recommend to its investors on 28 June 2018 to sell the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_part" title="Aircraft part">aircraft parts</a> with <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Aero" title="Volvo Aero">VA</a>S Aero Services within two years for 45 million USD, quickly for components like the <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a> or the <a
