href="/wiki/Auxiliary_power_unit" title="Auxiliary power unit">APU</a>.\n<a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Trent_900" title="Rolls-Royce Trent 900">Rolls-Royce Trent 900</a> leasing beyond March 2019 should generate 480,000 USD monthly for each aircraft before selling the turbofans by 2020.\nWith a total revenue of 80 million USD per aircraft, the overall <a href="/wiki/Return_on_capital" title="Return on capital">return</a> expected is 145-155% while 72% and 81% of their <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">debt</a> had already be repaid.<sup id="cite_ref-Dr.Peters5jun2018_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dr.Peters5jun2018-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BA wanted to replace its <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747s</a> but from 2021, Iran Air faced <a href="/wiki/Iran_deal" class="mw-redirect" title="Iran deal">political uncertainty</a> and Hi Fly did not have a convincing <a href="/wiki/Business_case" title="Business case">business case</a>.\nThe fifth plane coming back from SIA, owned by Amedeo (formerly Doric), may still go to Hi Fly.\nTwo others should return from Singapore Air in coming weeks but they could stay with an existing Asian A380 flag carrier.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg5jun2018_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg5jun2018-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>\nVAS Aero Services is a US aftermarket firm.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight5jun2018_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight5jun2018-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The teardown value includes $32-$33 million from the engines in 2020 and $4 million from leasing them till, while the value of a 2008 A380 would be $78.4 million in 2020 and its monthly <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_lease" title="Aircraft lease">lease</a> in 2018 would be $929,000.\nThe two aircraft have <a href="/wiki/Rate_of_return" title="Rate of return">returned</a> 3.8-4.2% per year since 2008 but the 145-155% return is lower than the 220% originally <a href="/wiki/Forecasting" title="Forecasting">forecast</a>.\nOf the nearly 500 made, 50 <a href="/wiki/747-400" class="mw-redirect" title="747-400">747-400s</a> were sold in the secondary market, including only 25 to new customers.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight7jun2018_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight7jun2018-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup>\nThese are among the first A380s delivered, lacking the improvements and weight savings of later ones.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orders_and_deliveries">Orders and deliveries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Orders and deliveries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A380_orders_and_deliveries" title="List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries">List of Airbus A380 orders and deliveries</a></div>\n<p>Eighteen customers have ordered the A380. Total orders for the A380 stand at 331 as of  May&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_O_D_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_O_D-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The biggest customer is Emirates, which has ordered or committed to order a total of 162 A380s.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_O_D_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_O_D-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> One <a href="/wiki/Very_Important_Person" class="mw-redirect" title="Very Important Person">VIP</a> order was made in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> but later cancelled by Airbus.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup>  The A380F version attracted 27 orders, before they were either cancelled (20) or converted to A380-800 (7) following the production delay and the subsequent suspension of the freighter program.\n</p><p>Delivery takes place in Hamburg for customers from Europe and the Middle East and in Toulouse for customers from the rest of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-A380_delivery_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380_delivery-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> EADS explained that deliveries in 2013 were to be slowed temporarily to accommodate replacement of the wing rib brackets where cracks were detected earlier in the existing fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, in expectation of raising the number of orders placed, <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> announced \'attractable discounts\' to airlines who placed large orders for the A380.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (June 2017)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Soon after, at the November 2013 <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Air_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubai Air Show">Dubai Air Show</a> where it ordered 150 <a href="/wiki/B777X" class="mw-redirect" title="B777X">B777X</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> ordered 50 aircraft, totalling $20 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, Airbus said that some ordered A380s might not be built for an undisclosed Japanese airline. <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">Qantas</a> planned to order eight more airplanes but is in doubt due to a cost-cutting drive. Amedeo, an aircraft lessor that ordered 20 A380s, had not found a client for the airliner as of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a> ordered six A380s in 2001 but never took delivery and later cancelled them in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of June 2017, Emirates has 48 orders outstanding but due to lack of space in <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubai Airport">Dubai Airport</a>, it deferred 12 deliveries by one year and will not take any in 2019-20 before replacing its early airliners from 2021: there are open production slots in 2019 and Airbus reduced its production rate at 12 per year for 2017-18. The real backlog is much smaller than the official 107 with 47 uncertain orders: 20 commitments for the A380-specialized lessor Amedeo which commits to production only once aircraft are placed, eight for Qantas which wants to keep its fleet at 12, six for Virgin Atlantic which does not want them anymore and three ex <a href="/wiki/Transaero" title="Transaero">Transaero</a> for finance vehicle Air Accord.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek9Jun2017_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek9Jun2017-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At its 100th delivery ceremony, Emirates Airline head <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_bin_Saeed_Al_Maktoum" title="Ahmed bin Saeed Al Maktoum">Ahmed bin Saeed Al Maktoum</a> was hoping to order new A380s at the November 2017 <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Air_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubai Air Show">Dubai Air Show</a> the following week.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup>\nEmirates does not need the small front staircase and eleven-abreast economy of the A380plus concept, but wants Airbus to commit to continue production for at least 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek14nov2017_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek14nov2017-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 18 January 2018, Airbus secured a preliminary agreement from Emirates for up to 36 A380s: 20 potentially firm orders and 16 options, to be delivered from 2020, valued at $16 billion at list prices.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup>\nJohn Leahy is confident that Airbus will secure one more A380 order in 2018; discussions are reportedly under way with IAG for British Airways to take new A380s, which could be cheaper than refurbishing second-hand planes to its specifications.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg19jan2018_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg19jan2018-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:1em 1em 1em 300; border:1px #aaa solid; font-size:95%; background-color:#fbf8db; text-align:center;">\n<caption>A380 firm net orders and deliveries\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr style="font-weight:bold; background-color:#ccddff; padding:0.3em;">\n<td><div class="plainlinks hlist orders and deliveries</b><br />\n</p>\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_cf7f275c77ae0aca8c203f2f3242c7c7"></map><img usemap="#timeline_cf7f275c77ae0aca8c203f2f3242c7c7" .25em;">&#8195;</span>Orders</p><div style="clear:both;"></div> <p><span style="background:green; padding:0em .1em; border:solid 1px #242020; height:1.5em; margin:.25em .9em .25em .25em;">&#8195;</span>Deliveries</p><div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p><br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operators">Operators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span on 27 December 2014<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hi_Fly_(airline)" title="Hi Fly (airline)">Hi Fly</a> first service on 1 August 2018<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_routes">Notable routes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable routes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The shortest regular commercial route that the A380 flies is from <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hamad_International_Airport" title="Hamad International Airport">Doha</a> (379&#160;km or 236 miles) with Emirates<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> (As of 6 June 2017, this route has been suspended due to deterioration of diplomatic relationship between the two countries<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup>). Air France briefly operated the A380 on the shorter <a href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris Charles de Gaulle</a> to <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow</a> route (344&#160;km or 214 miles) in mid-2010.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> The longest A380 route, and <a href="/wiki/Longest_flights" title="Longest flights">the third longest non-stop commercial flight in the world</a>, is flown by Emirates from <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a> to <a href="/wiki/Auckland_Airport" title="Auckland Airport">Auckland</a> at 14,203 kilometres (8,825&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The A380 has been involved in two <a href="/wiki/Aviation_accidents_and_incidents" title="Aviation accidents and incidents">aviation occurrences</a> and no <a href="/wiki/Hull_loss" title="Hull loss">hull loss</a> <a href="/wiki/Aviation_accidents_and_incidents" title="Aviation accidents and incidents">accidents</a> with no fatalities as of  October&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.\n</p>\n<ul><li>On 4 November 2010, <a href="/wiki/Qantas_Flight_32" title="Qantas Flight 32">Qantas Flight 32</a>, en route from <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Changi_Airport" title="Singapore Changi Airport">Singapore Changi Airport</a> to <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Airport" title="Sydney Airport">Sydney Airport</a>, suffered an <a href="/wiki/Uncontained_engine_failure" class="mw-redirect" title="Uncontained engine failure">uncontained engine failure</a>, resulting in a series of related problems, and forcing the flight to make an <a href="/wiki/Emergency_landing" title="Emergency landing">emergency landing</a>. The plane safely returned to Singapore. There were no injuries to the passengers, crew or people on the ground despite debris falling onto the Indonesian island of <a href="/wiki/Batam" title="Batam">Batam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-abc3057573_updated_365-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc3057573_updated-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> The A380 was damaged sufficiently for the event to be classified as an accident.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> Qantas subsequently grounded all of its A380s that day subject to an internal investigation taken in conjunction with the engine manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolls-Royce plc">Rolls-Royce plc</a>. A380s powered by <a href="/wiki/Engine_Alliance" title="Engine Alliance">Engine Alliance</a> GP7000 were unaffected but operators of <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Trent_900" title="Rolls-Royce Trent 900">Rolls-Royce Trent 900</a>-powered A380s were affected. Investigators determined that an oil leak, caused by a defective oil supply pipe, led to an engine fire and subsequent uncontained engine failure.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> Repairs cost an estimated <span style="white-space: nowrap">A$</span>139 million (~US$145M).<sup id="cite_ref-back-in-the-air_368-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-back-in-the-air-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup> As other Rolls-Royce Trent 900 engines also showed problems with the same oil leak, Rolls-Royce ordered many engines to be changed, including about half of the engines in the Qantas A380 fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup> During the airplane\'s repair, cracks were discovered in wing structural fittings which also resulted in mandatory inspections of all A380s and subsequent design changes.<sup id="cite_ref-EASA_Wing_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EASA_Wing-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<ul><li>On 30 September 2017, <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_66" title="Air France Flight 66">Air France Flight 66</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Engine_Alliance_GP7000#Variants" title="Engine Alliance GP7000">Engine Alliance GP7270</a> powered Airbus A380, registration F-HPJE, suffered an apparent uncontained engine failure while operating from <a href="/wiki/Paris_Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport</a> to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> The aircraft safely diverted to <a href="/wiki/CFB_Goose_Bay" title="CFB Goose Bay">CFB Goose Bay</a>, Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications">Specifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A380&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Specifications">edit</a><span Designed by Airbus and co-developed with Thales and Diehl Aerospace, the IMA is a leap-ahead technological innovation, with all onboard computing modules networked and able to support different applications.
